BIOMAC weekly hangout meetings  
During the preparation period of BIOMAC OITB and considering the travel limitations due to the COVID19 
outbreak all partners participated to the have weekly hangout meetings which were organized for the better 
planning of the interconnected and multidisciplinary proposal tasks. Partners representatives (~80 close to 90 
weekly) participated in web meetings (using Hangouts application)  contributing though fruitful discussions 
updates on the content of the proposal and further developments to be included in the context of the proposal. 
Further to this , separate individual group calls among the partners took place to better facilitate the different 
aspects related to the Pilot Line Clusters, the services Hubs the definition of Test Cases, the administrative and 
operational setup of the BIOMAC ecosystem, as well as other issues regarding the workflow s and other 
organizational matters.

4.1 Participants  
4.1.1 ARISTOTELIO PANEPISTIMIO THESSALONIKIS  
Short Name AUTH Type  RTD Country GR 
 
 
www.auth.gr, www.chem.auth.gr 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
The Aristotle University of Thessaloniki (AUTH) is an academic Institution which is composed of 11 faculties 
consisting of 36 Schools and involves a critical mass of Faculty approximately equal to 40000 active students (31000 
undergraduate and 9,000 postgradua te of which 3952 at doctorate level) and 2366 faculty members. AUTH is the 
largest University in Greece and in the Balkans and in terms of promoting innovation, 32 patents have been granted 
during the last 3 years on a national, European and international level. Based on recent data from international 
ranking lists, of 20372 higher institutions in the world, AUTH from the 407th position in 2011 moved to the 158th 
in 2012, ranking first among 23 Greek Universities. AUTH has a funding (2009 -2013) (nationally and 
internationally) for the three major faculties: Health, Sciences and Engineering of a total of 138,330,059 million of 
euros, with the faculty of science having 38,153,623 million of euros. It is also worth to mention that AUTH has 864 
international partners and 2355 active research programs (year 2013) and showing an enhancement the last years not 
only to funding but also in international cooperation. The School of Chemistry (Faculty of Sciences) established at 
the AUTh in 1927. From the School of chemistry, an undergraduate programme can lead to different specializations 
of i) theoretical chemistry and chemical education, ii) chemical analysis-environmental chemistry-electrochemistry, 
iii) chemical synthesis-biochemistry and bioapplications and iv) chemical technology and industrial chemistry. The 
school has also 11 postgraduate studies, covering the area of chemistry and a vast areas of other sciences. The school 
has 78 faculty members and 10 laboratories. Finally, it has to be noted the EChemTest® whic h is an electronic 
selfassessment and assessment tool developed by the European Chemistry Thematic Network Association, and 
aimed at evaluating knowledge and competences in chemical subjects. It has a wide-ranging impact, both formal and 
informal, in Europe and outside its borders. In the present proposal, two Laboratories will be involved, the Laboratory 
of Chemical and Environmental Technology (LCET) and the Laboratory of Polymer Chemistry and Technology 
(LPCT). LCET has expertise and infrastructure on th ermochemical and (bio)catalytic processes for biomass 
valorisation to fuels, chemicals and materials. LPCT focuses on (bio)polymer and (bio)composites synthesis and 
characterization, as well as applications of (bio)polymers in several areas including pipes, films, bottles, fibers, etc. 
Role in the Project 
 
PL3 (AUTH, GR):  Sugar derived polyols and diols by catalytic hydrogenation/hydrogenolysis 
 
AUTH will be the coordinator of the project leading WP10 as well as undertaking the scheduled activities described 
in detail in Section 3. AUTH will have a central role in the management activities of the project and will be 
responsible for the communication with the European Commission. AUTH will contribute to the BIOMAC project 
with PL3: Sugar derived polyols and diols by catalytic hydrogenation/hydrogenolysis. Further to this, AUTH has a 
vital role inWP2 where they will implement the upgrade and modifications of their Pilot Line. Collaborating with 
other PL owners they will be involved in Task 3.2 for Automotive Test Case, producing monomers of polyols (sugars 
alcohols) and glycols/diols for the value chain of succinate based polyester and polyurethane resins. Additionally, 
they will contribute to Task 3.3 that deals with the production of Agricultural Mulch Films Test Case where the 
glucose rich streams delivered from PL5 & 6 will be further converted to monomer polyols and diols by AUTH to 
be used for the production of succinate based polyesters. Monomer polyols/diols will be also provided by AUTH in 
Task 3.6, for the Test Case of Printed Electronics. In WP4 (Task 4.2), AUTH will support activities related to the 
characterization of materials and products. In WP7 they will lead Task 7.3, where the selection of additional test 
cases will be addressed fitting the Ecosystem capacities. Finally, AUTH will be involved in activities regarding the 
exploitation and dissemination of the BIOMAC ecosystem in the context of WP8 & 9.

Infrastructure & technical equipment 
Infrastructure for the thermochemical and catalytic valorization of biomass:  
Equipment for catalyst preparation: Autoclaves for hydrothermal synthesis, Ultrasound baths, Tube/muffle furnaces 
with controlled atmosphere, Rotary evaporators, freeze dryers, ball milling, spray dryer, etc..   
Equipment for catalyst characterization:  Fast response unit for TPR, TPO, TPD measurements, DRIFTS cell for in 
situ IR measurements of catalysts, under reaction conditions, N2 porosimetry, FTIR spectrometer, 
Thermogravimetric analyzer (TGA), X -Ray Diffrac tometer (XRD), Scanning Electron Microscope (SEM), 
Transmission Electron Microscope (TEM), Coupled Plasma Atomic Adsorption Spectrometer (ICP-AES), UV-Vis 
Spectrometer, Solid state MAS-NMR, X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS), etc.   
Equipment for catal ytic reactions and processes: Fully equipped high pressure (autoclaves) batch reactors, 
continuous flow (fixed and fluid bed) atmospheric and high-pressure reactor units at the lab/micro-pilot scale.  
Equipment for reaction products analysis and liquid fuels testing: HPLC, GS -MC, GC -FID/TCD, LC -MS/MS, 
Py/GC_MS, NMR, Bomb calorimeter, Flash point (closed cup) tester, Distillation units (ASTM D-86) for light and 
middle distillates, Pour and cloud point tester, Densitometers, Distillation unit (ASTM D-1160) for heavy distillates, 
etc.

Polymer Chemistry and Technology: Synthesis, characterization, properties (thermal, mechanical etc.) and 
applications of polymers. Polymer Recycling. Polymer modification and improvement of final properties by using 
various additives. Mathematical modelling of polymerization and decomposition reactions. Chemistry and

Persons Involved 
Name Dimitrios Bikiaris 
Position Prof. Title Dr. Gender Male 
Short 
CV 
Dimitrios N. Bikiaris (http://dbic.webpages.auth.gr/) is a Professor at the Chemistry Department of 
AUTH since 2015. His research interests include the synthesis and characterization of polyesters, the 
development of polymers using biobased monomers, the synthesis and characterization of copolymers, 
the preparation and study of composite and nanocomposite polymeric materials with various polymeric 
matrices, the surface modification of nanoparticles, the recycling of polymers with various techniques 
(melt extrusion, microwave irradiation, hydrolysis, etc.,) modification of natural polymers, use of 
polymers to remove contaminants (heavy metals, drugs, pigments, etc.) from urban and industrial sites, 
etc. His scientific work has been published in more than 325 scientific papers in international scientific 
journals, with over 13000 references, and h-index 56 (scopus). He participated in 44 research projects, 
in 20 of which he was scientifically responsible. He has also written 4 chapters in international scientific 
books and he holds 15 international patents and 2 Greek. His research team currently consists of about 
16 researchers (2 post-doctoral students, 5 doctoral candidates, 4 postgraduate students and 5 
undergraduate students). He has developed strong collaborations with researchers from International 
Universities and Research Centers. He has also significant collaborations with professors and researchers 
from Greek Universities.  Finally, in the framework of joint research projects and interests, he has 
developed collaborations with several companies such as: Pharmathen S.A., Interplast S.A., KARINA 

DT-NMBP-04-2020    
 
[BIOMAC]   [8 of 115] 
SA, CHIMAR Hellas SA, Plastics Crete SA, Loufakis Chemicals SA, Medicair S.A., Hatzopoulos S.A., 
Papaplast S.A. 
He has participated in more than 150 international and 50 national conferences, having 80 oral 
presentations as a simple and invited speaker, and 190 poster presentations. He has been a reviewer in 
more than 120 international journals and member of editorial committees in eight scientific journals. He 
also participated as an assessor in Greek and European research projects (FP7 and Horizon 2020) and as 
a reviewer in research programs of several European countries (UK, Cyprus, Poland, Czech Republic, 
Slovakia, Slovenia, Spain, etc.). In 2008 he was included among the top 100 scientists in the field of 
Chemistry and Polymer Technology from the International Bibliographic Center. In December 2017 he 
was honored as the best researcher with an Excellence Award from the Aristotle University of 
Thessaloniki for his scientific work in both Natural and Engineering Sciences, based on the number of 
published papers and the h index. He is also a member of the scientific committee of Prix Galien Greece 
Prize, awarded to Greek sc ientists who have significantly contributed to innovation through the 
development of innovative ideas, products or methods for the diagnosis or treatment of diseases.

CV 
Dr Margaritis Kostoglou is a faculty member (professor) at the dept. of Chemistry at the Aristotle 
University of Thessaloniki, Greece from 2004. He has a Diploma in Chemical Engineer from Aristotle 
University of Thessaloniki (1989) and a PhD from the Department of Chemical Engineering of the same 
university (1995). He worked as a Researcher in Center of Research and Technology Hellas (CERTH) 
(1996-2001) and as Engineering in Ministry of Defense (2002-2004). His main research interests are in: 
fundamentals of chemical technology processes; analysis of transport phenomena; analysis, description, 
design and optimization of unit operations; mathematical modeling of physicochemical processes in 
several scales. A large part of his work is devoted to particulate processes either for fluid particles and 
interfaces (bubbles/droplets) or for solid particles (colloidal particles/nanoparticles/aerosols) and to heat 
transfer from fundamentals to applications. Author of more than 200 journal publications and more than 
220 conference presentations. His work has received more than 2600 heterocitations. He has participated 
in more than 45 European, national or industrial research programs.  He has been reviewer for 90 
Scientific Journals.

4.1.2 EUROPEAN BIOMASS INDUSTRY ASSOCIATION (EUBIA) 
Short Name EUBIA Type  Association Country BE 
 
 
http://www.eubia.org  
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
EUBIA, the European Biomass Industry Association, was established in 1996 as an international non-profit association 
in Brussels, Belgium. It groups together market actors, technology providers, and knowledge centres, all of them active 
in the field of biomass. The main objective of EUBIA is to support the European biomass industries at all levels, 
promoting the use of biomass as an energy source, developing innovative bioenergy concepts and fostering international 
co-operation within the bioenergy field. As an industrial association, EUBIA aims at helping small and medium 
enterprises (SMEs) to keep up with relevant technolo gical legal developments. EUBIA acts as an information 
multiplier, disseminating technologies and know-how to SMEs across the entire biomass industry. EUBIA also acts as 
an aggregator of demand, identifying shared problems and ensuring that research focuse s on real business needs. 
EUBIA is co -organizer of the European Biomass Conference and Exhibition, the largest biomass event in Europe, 
taking place every year and gathering hundreds of stakeholders and experts. 
Role in the Project 
EUBIA is a European Association supporting the European biomass industries at all levels. As an association they will 
immobilize their members and assist BEECO on mapping of biomass sources across Europe. In BIOMAC Project 
EUBIA will be the leader of WP9, dealing wi th dissemination and communication activities of the project. More 
specifically, in Task 9.1 they will work on D&C activities and t he preparation of  D&C strategy that will  intend to 
reach a wide audience and communicate the Pilot lines and services, novel ties and knowledge provided by the 
ecosystem. Clustering activities will also be part of this WP, seeking the widest engagement of stakeholders in the 
activities of BIOMAC (Task 9.2) and attracting investors and future clients . To further promote the new k nowledge

4.1.3 BIO ECO ENERGY COMPANY D.O.O. 
Short Name BEECO Type  Association Country CRO 
 
 
WWW.BEECO.HR 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
Bio Eco Energy Company d.o.o. (BEECO) commercially cultivates Miscanthus x giganteus  (MxG) and develops 
sustainable biomass feedstock supply chains in Croatia. BEECO has the vision to become a leading producer/distributor 
of Miscanthus x giganteus planting material and supplier of cellulosic biomass feedstock in the Western Balkans region. 
BEECO distributes the woody, rhizomatous C4 perennial grass Miscanthus x giganteus as the “King of fiber”,  - the 
best crop for energy farming, biomass energy generation, biofuels, and chemicals pr oduction. BEECO implements 
sustainable technologies and provides turnkey solutions for biomass energy generation projects as far, as a range of 
comprehensive services: from energy crops plantation establishment and energy farming to vertically integrated clean-
tech biomass energy systems. BEECO is a full member of the Bio-based Industries JU and the Bioenergy Europe.  
Role in the Project 
BEECO is a provider of biomass valorised for various industries such as biofuels, chemical, pharmaceutical, textile, 
paper, and carpentry industry. In BIOMAC in WP3, they will provide cellulosic biomass feedstock from MxG for: 
• Task 3.2. Bio -based resins reinforc ed with NL and NFC as UV -curing materials for AM. Properties to be 
achieved, high temperature. stability, low weight, and high ductility for interior applications.   
• Task 3.3. Succinic acid as a bio-monomer and NFC will consist formulation of bioplastics for application into 
biodegradable in soil mulch films. This will improve mechanical properties in soil mulch films and will be 
tested on the field (in cooperation with farmers) in combination with biochar/compost. 
• Task 3.4. Surface nanotexturing employed for tailored nano-structuring. Vacuum thermoforming will be post 
utilized for the production of food containers, biobased PLA foils reinforced with NL and BNC will pass the 
thermoforming PL of NNT. PLA & NFC based inks and coating for improving  the barrier and mechanical 
properties of flexible packaging materials. 
• Task 3.5. Footbridge module 2mx0.45mx0.65m., biomaterial functionalities are UV and fire resistance >80ºC, 
anti-fouling & easy -cleaning capability. Manufactured by multi-material AM modified by NFC, NCN, and 
Biochar embedded in thermoplastic isocyanide free biopolymers of TPU. 
• Task 3.6. Biobased inks will be developed reinforced by functionalized nanocellulose using bioresins, TPU, 
and nano copper for stretchable electrical prints integrated directly into textiles. 
Relevant publications, products to the project 
BEECO has provided: 
• Selling first-class certified F2 rhizomes planting material of Miscanthus x giganteus clone Illinois, 
• Consultancy services for farmers and growers, 
• Feedstock supply chain solutions for the end-user (cogeneration facilities, biorefinery facilities, biogas 
facilities, pulp & paper production facilities, biomaterial production facilities, etc.), 
• Full logistic support and services for establishing a private biomass plantation for the end-user, 
• Commercial planting, growing harvesting and storage of Miscanthus giganteus biomass for the end-user. 
Previous Projects 
The basic role of the BEECO company is the production  and supply of sustainable biomass feedstock on a commercial 
scale. The BEECO company is the pioneer in the production of sustainable energy crops of industrial scale, most 
notably Miscanthus Giganteus, being the only Croatian company involved in this kind of activity to date. We have been 
operating since 2016 and are the owner of the biggest Miscanthus nursery plantation in Europe. The team involved in 
this bid is well experienced with substantial knowledge and skills in managing the energy crops production as well as 
providing turn-key solutions. This will be of critical importance for taking out this project since it requires biomass 
feedstock of the highest quality and in the optimal quantities. This feedstock can be grown on marginal lands and thus 
present non -food competing production. Additionally, our experts have all the necessary experience and skills to 
provide technical assistance for taking out the BEECO applicable project activities.   
Infrastructure & technical equipment 
BEECO’s office is in the center of Zagreb, the capital of Croatia. Our nursery plantation (25 ha) is located near the 
town of Popovača, Sisak-moslavačka County.

4.1.4  Luleå University of Technology  
Short Name LTU Type  RTD Country SE 
 
 
 
https://www.ltu.se/  
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
The Biochemical Process Engineering research group at LTU  (Division of Chemical Engineering, Department of 
Civil, Environmental and Natural Resources Engineering) consists of 20 people working with biomass pretreatment, 
design and use of enzymes and microorganisms for production of fuels, chemicals and materials from lignocellulose 
materials. Their expertise ranges from molecular biology, meta bolic engineering, microbial physiology, 
fermentation, enzyme discovery and technology, protein chemistry, process technology to modeling of bioprocesses. 
The research group is working in the field of microbial and chemoenzymatic production of fuels and chemicals since 
1989. Ethanol, butanol, butyric acid, butyl butyrate, biogas, lipids, prebiotic cello - and xylo -oligosaccharides, 
antioxidants, novel enzyme activities, biocatalysis in non-conventional media, using fungi, yeasts, bacteria and algae 
are the group’s recent key activities. Moreover, a recently installed steam explosion/organosolv reactor, upgraded to 
a semi-continuous system, that also allows the solid/liquid separation to take place at high temperature and pressure 
, allows the group to study t he fractionation of lignocellulosics for different applications such as lignin catalytic 
conversion to aromatic monomers, production of lignin nanoparticles,  use of lignin/(poly) ethylene glycol mixtures 
as anti-wear agents, use  of lignin/ethylene glycol mixtures as marine fuels and also use of delignified  carbohydrate 
fraction for the production of ethanol and lipids using yeasts and microalgae as microbial platforms. 
Role in the Project 
 
PL1 (LTU, SE): Semi-continuous organosolv-steam explosion pre-treatment PL 
 
LTU is involved in BIOMAC with the provision of pilot line (PL 1): Semi-continuous organosolv-steam explosion 
pre-treatment. This PL will allow solid/liquid separation. More specifically, LTU will contribute in WP2 on the 
upgrading of the existing pilot line of organosolv fractionation, modify and upgrade the semi-continuous reactor to 
operate in a sully continuous mode by adding a continuous feeder, test and verify the new equipment, fractionate 
selected biomass feedstock and provide with fractions of cellulose, hemicellulose and lignin for further processing. 
LTU will also support the work conducted in Task 3.2 towards the production of bio-based resins, Task 3.4 for the 
production of food packaging and Task 3.6 for the production of biobased inks. The above-mentioned developments 
are included in the Test Cases 1,3 and 5 in the sectors of Automotive Food, Packaging and Printed Electronics 
respectively. Finally, LTU will support the OITB clustering activities at Task 9.2, the administrative and financial 
project management at task 10.1 and technical project management at Task 10.2.

4.1.5 Bio Base Europe - Pilot Plant 
Shot Name BBEPP Type RTD Country BE 
 
http://bbeu.org/ 
 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
Bio Base Europe Pilot Plant (www.bbeu.org) is a flexible and diversified pilot plant for the development and scale 
up of new, bio -based and sustainable processes. It is capable of development of new bioprocesses, optimization of 
existing processes and scale up of a broad variety of bio-based processes up to an industrial level (from 5L to 50m 3 
scale, depending on the process). It can perform the entire value chain, from the green resources up to the final product. 
BBEU intends to close the gap in the innovation chain of the bio -based economy, bridging science and industrial 
production. BBEU was selected by the European Commission as a multi -KET Pilot Lines demonstrator 
(www.mkpl.eu). It is located in Ghent, Belgium. 
The activities of BBEU can be categorized in: 
• Development of bio-based and sustainable processes (TRL 2-4) 
• Scale up (TRL 5-6) 
• Pilot and demo production to allow market introduction (TRL 7-8) 
The BBEU team combines over 100 years of experience in fermentation development and scale -up, and also has 
extensive expertise in biom ass pretreatment, biocatalysis, green chemistry, and the development of industrial 
purification techniques. It is responsible for these tasks in several publicly funded projects of which 24 are ongoing. 
In addition, BBEU is a service provider to many compa nies in the biotech domain and bio -based economy. In the 
period 2012-2019 it served > 120 customers in > 300 projects for development, scale up or pilot production. 
BBEU has built up a significant expertise in the pretreatment of various biomasses such as lignin, forestry waste, tree 
bark in projects such as Biohart, Falcon, Rehap and Erifore. For performing these processes, Bio Base Europe Pilot 
Plant has 4 process halls, and a supporting lab for analysis: a biomass pre-treatment hall of 907m2 with hydrolysis 
reactors, milling equipment, jet cooking, centrifuges, presses and evaporators; a fermentation hall of 500 m2 for 
industrial biotechnology processes and product purification (centrifugation, filtration, ion exchange, crystallization, 
extraction, drying  equipment). An ATEX-proof ‘green process hall’  of 285 m2 is available for working with 
solvents, green chemistry and anaerobic fermentations. Since 2018, a new 1600 m2 process hall for biorefining and 
downstream processing  with reactors, filtration units, dryers, etc. was placed into operation. A full list of the 
equipment at BBEPP can be found at http://www.bbeu.org/pilotplant/bbepp-expertise-folders/. 
Role in the Project 
 
PL5 (BBEPP, BE): Hydrothermal pre-treatment of biomass 
PL6: (BBEPP, BE): Recovery / Separation   
 
Bio Base Europe Pilot Plant will be one of the partners where 2 physical pilot lines will be installed. More specifically, 
Pilot Line 5, where monomers from lignin and hemicellulose like materials will be obtained in flexible high pressure 
reactors via either a continuous process, or via batch wise hydrolysis using sulphuric acid as a catalyst. Particularly, 
in WP3 , Task 3.1  that deals with the  Agricultural Test Case, BBEPP PL for the biomass 
pretreatment/fractionationation will be operated providing lignin and cellulose. Additionally, in Task 3.3, BBEPP PL5 
will start with the Pre-treatment of biomass delivering Lignin that will be used as received for the Reactive Extrusion 
the second fraction will be the Cellulose which will be converted to nanocellusole and biochar. BBEU will be mainly 
involved in WP2 regarding the upgrade of Pilot Lines as well as in WP5 for the market uptake of BIOMAC Ecosystem.  
Relevant publications, products to the project 
Publications: 
BBEPP, through its experience in bio based pilot project, has provided several relevant services to  
industries, research institutes and public bodies:  
- Technology development & demonstration based on agro residues  
- Tutorial for market introduction of novel molecules produced via Industrial Biotech from renewable resources  
- Policy recommendations on how to organise & support pilot activities within the industrial biotech & bio economy 
to bridge the valley of death  
 
Specific awards and certifications:  

DT-NMBP-04-2020    
 
[BIOMAC]   [19 of 115] 
BBEPP was selected in 2014 by the European Commission as a multi-KET Pilot Lines demonstrator  
Previous Projects 
1.Rehap: Horizon 2020-Spire-2016: Transform agroforestry waste into High Added-value Products. REHAP aims at 
converting agricultural (wheat straw) and forestry (bark) waste into building blocks (1,4 and 2,3 -Butanediol, 
estherpolyols), materials (polyurethanes, phenolic resins, modified hyd rolysis lignin) and products (wooden boards, 
insulation foams, cement, adhesive). The developed processing technologies such as fermentation and chemical, 
thermal and enzymatic conversions, will be optimized at pilot scale (TRL6-7).  
 
2.Biohart:  Interreg VL-NL: Biorizon Innovation and Upscaling of Renewable Aromatics Technology. Over the past 
years Biorizon has developed three commercially promising technologies for the conversion of wood, sugars and 
lignin into aromatics. By demonstrating the technology w ithin this project on a larger scale, the confidence in the 
applicability of the technology on an industrial scale enhances and the risk to invest diminishes. Simultaneously bio-
aromatics will be produced in sufficient quantities to be able to start applic ation development routes.In 2018, The 
BIO-HArT project was one of the winners of the European ‘Let the Stars Shine’ initiative. With this initiative, nine 
members of the European Parliament want to highlight fine examples of European projects in order to g ain 
enthousiasm and support for European cooperation. A BIO-HArT video made within the ‘Let the Stars Shine’ context. 
 
3.ERIFORE: H2020-Infradev-1-2014-1: Research Infrastructure for Circular Forest Bioeconomy. ERIFORE aims to 
establish an open access rese arch infrastructure for circular forest bioeconomy across Europe. This will unlock the 
full potential of available forest biomass and will give rise to a new level of co -operation between the major RTD 
providers in the field. To achieve this, the project will first assess: (1) The sources of forest derived biomass and their 
availability and (2) The existing expertise and equipment of the project partners on the processing steps to convert 
forest biomass into valuable end products. 
 
4.Falcon: H2020-NMBP-BIO-2016: Fuel And chemicals from Lignin through enzymatic and chemical CONversion. 
FALCON aims to convert lignin -rich industrial waste of 2G biofuel plants to higher value products, in particular 
shipping fuels, fuel additives and chemical building blocks. This would be the next consecutive step in turning waste 
to products, thus minimizing waste and simultaneously providing new alternatives for fossil resource based processes. 
The FALCON process is based on enzymatic and mild chemical conversio n of the lignin waste stream, providing a 
more environmentally friendly approach to the production of fuels and chemical building blocks. 
Infrastructure & technical equipment 
The Bio Base Europe Plant is located in the harbour of Ghent, Belgium. An overview of the available equipment can 
be found at http://www.bbeu.org/pilotplant/bbepp-expertise-folders/.

4.1.6 Luxembourg Institute of Science & Technology 
Short Name LIST Type  RTO Country LU 
 
 
http://www.list.lu/ 
 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
The Luxembourg Institute of Science and Technology (LIST) is a mission -driven Research and Technology 
Organization (RTO) that develops advanced technologies and delivers innovative products and services to industry 
and society. As a major engine of the diversi fication and growth of Luxembourg’s economy through innovation, 
LIST supports the deployment of a number of solutions to a wide range of sectors, including energy, IT, 
telecommunications, environment, agriculture, and advanced manufacturing at national and European level. 
It is formed by three departments: 
• The “Environmental Research & Innovation” (ERIN) department develops strategies, technologies and tools 
to monitor, assess, use and safeguard natural and renewable resources. Its research topics are water security 
and safety, plants for biomass, biopolymers and bioenergy, life cycle sustainability and risk assessment, and 
e-Science for environmental and biological applications. 
• The “IT for Innovative Services” (ITIS) department develops innovative IT services within an open 
innovation process integrating all stakeholders concerned. Its research focuses on “big data” operational 
issues for decision making, use of information systems in measuring and controlling the quality of services, 
and tools for innovation processes in IT services. 
• The “Materials Research and Technology” (MRT) department focuses its activities on advanced materials 
and nanotechnologies. MRT translates cutting edge materials research into applicable technology. For this, 
the department cultivates close relationships and joint projects with both academic and industrial partners, 
and contributes to Luxembourg's and Europe's innovation agenda in materials research. Its research and 
technology activities target two main areas: nanomaterial s and nanotechnology, and functional 
(bio)composite materials. Biobased polymers and related biocomposites is one of the fields in which the 
MRT department is growing.  
Role in the Project 
 
PL9 (LIST, LU) Continuous Reactive Extrusion for TPU 
PL10 (LIST, LU): Mechanical milling and Production of different grades of nanofibrillated cellulose NFCs 
 
LIST is offering two pilot lines related to i) reactive extrusion that will be used to synthesize isocyanate -free 
thermoplastic polyurethanes (TPU) from di fferent polyols such oligosaccharides, lignin etc . where also different 
nanofillers will be compounded either in-situ during the course of the polymerization or afterward (PL9: Continuous 
Reactive Extrusion for TPU) and ii) the pilot line for the production of different grades of nanofibrillated cellulose 
(NFCs) using mechanical treatment (Super  Mass Colloider) and using various starting cellulosic material having 
different compositions (PL10: Mechanical milling and  Production of different grades of nanofibrillated cellulose 
NFCs). LIST will lead the WP3 related to the Pilot Plant Supreme Hub Services. Under this WP LIST will handle 
Task 3.1: Preparation of Specifications and protocols of the different pilot lines and contribute to the other tasks 
under this WP . In addition, LIST will be involved in Task 1 0.2 related to the t echnical project management. Dr 
Habibi will act as the Technical Validation Manager for the Ecosystem

Infrastructure & technical equipment 
The technical platform at the LIST is highly adequate to ensure a successful conduction of the tasks. LIST offers a 
world class working conditions including office spaces and a state-of-the-art laboratories and a unique experimental 
infrastructure that be applied to organic polymeric nanocomposites: 
Synthesis and preparation: fully equipped chemistry labs to synthesize small molecules, nanoparticles and polymers 
from small quantities to large scale. They are set with high vacuum gas manifold (Schlenk line), polycondensation 
reactors, ionic polymerisation reactors, solvent purification lines, spray drying. Dedicated labs for nanopowders 
handling (CleanRoom Class 100 and Class 10). 
Monomer/polymer processing:  
All scales are accessible for both liquid monomers and polymer melts, allowing scale -up/downs of all reactive 
extrusion process from grams to hundreds of kilograms.  
• Equipment dedicated to monomer reaction: microfluidizer and infusion process. 
• Equipment for both monomer and polymer (reactive) modification: Micro-, mini- and large extruders (batch 
or continuous), internal (batch) mixers 
• For the post processing of polymers/resin include: compression moulding, micro -injection, infusion, 3D 
printers (FDM and SLS).  
 
 
Figure: reactive extrusion (a) 18 mm twin-screw extruders used for reactive extrusion (from 25 to 450 °C) completed by 
flexible set-up. Variety of screw profiles (up to 60 L/D), feeders (5 solid feeders, 2 liquid feeders), de -volatilization, cooling 
belt, water bath and grinders. This equipment has the ability to process monomers/polymers from 250 to 10000 g/h under 
shearing (speed range up to 1200 rpm). (b) possibility to combine extruders together in tandem   
Natural Fiber Processing:  
SuperMassColloider from Masuka for the mechanical treatment of cellulosic fibers.

Dr Youssef Habibi is Lead Scientist at the Luxembourg Institute of Science and Technology 
(LIST). He received his Ph.D. in polymer chemistry from Joseph Fourier University (Grenoble, 
France) prepared jointly with Centre de Recherche sur les Macromolecules Végétales 
(CERMAV). Before joining LIST, he worked in chronological order as Research and Teaching 
Assistant at the French Engineering School of Paper, Printing and Biomaterials (PAGORA, 
Grenoble Institute of Technology, France), as Research Assistant Professor at Department of 
Forest Biomaterials at North Carolina State University (NCSU, Raleigh, USA) and as Senior 
Scientist at 'Service des Matériaux Polymers et Composites' at University of Mons (Belgium). 
Dr Habibi is working across many branches of polymer and green chemistries for the sustainable 
production of polymeric materials. His research interests include biomass conversion 
technologies, the design of new (bio)polymers, the isolation, processing and surface chemical 
modification of biobased nanofillers such as nanocellulose , the development of functional and 
high-performance nanocomposites and coatings. He has published over 130 research articles or 
invited reviews in high-standard peer review journals and (co)edited and/or (co)authored several 
books and/or book chapters (H-index = 47, number of citations 14719 according to google scholar 
citations as for 31/03/2020).

4.1.7 RISE Processum AB 
Short Name Processum Type  RTD Country SE 
 
 
http://www.processum.se 
 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
RISE Processum AB is a research institute located in Örnsköldsvik, Sweden. It is part of the governmentally owned 
RISE (Research Institutes of Sweden, 60% ownership in RISE Processum). RISE Processum supports and initiates 
research and development mostly within the biorefinery sector. Together with partners from the industry and 
academia we act as a hub for development of new products, processes and energy solutions from the forest and 
residual streams from the process industry. The competence at RISE Processum, the pilot park of equipment designed 
for working with biorefinery processes, industrial experience and network of partners create a research hub within 
the biorefinery field. The organization with scientists and experts with complementing experiences are front runners 
in the development of new techniqu es, methods and products that can be directly applied by the industry. RISE 
Processum has gained expertise in several areas of research through participation in a large number of research 
projects. These areas include, among others, single cell protein production, lactic acid fermentation, bacterial protein 
expression, enzymatic hydrolysis, bacterial nanocellulose production, high temperature/pressure processes and 
lignin valorization processes. In addition, there is broad experience at RISE Processum within project management, 
communication, networking, patent and IPR-management and handling. 
The biotechnology group at RISE Processum are focusing on projects where biotechnology methods are applied to 
develop new processes and products from forest raw materi al. Enzymes and microorganisms like bacteria, yeast, 
algae and fungi are used as important tools for turning lignocellulose and industrial side streams to valuable products 
such as fuel, chemicals, materials and proteins. The biotechnology group has access  to well-equipped laboratories 
for laboratory scale optimization. For upscaling of processes there are pilot scale equipment at hand for 
thermochemical pretreatment, enzymatic hydrolysis, separation and fermentation up to 600 litres per batch. The pilot 
equipment is approved for genetically modified organisms. In addition, there is equipment available for molecular 
biology research applications. 
The organic chemistry group at RISE Processum are working in several fields, among which are chemical synthesis, 
flow chemistry and hydrothermal liquefaction and carbonization. For large scale process development there is an 
ATEX-facility at hand where processes can be performed batch -wise or continuously. For downstream processing 
there are pilot equipment for filtration, extraction, de-watering, distillation and upgrading. 
Role in the Project 
 
PL2 (RISE, SE): Hydrolysis of fibre sludge and BNC production. 
 
RISE is the Swedish Research Institute and innovation partner that offers unique expertise and about 100 testbeds 
and demonstration facilities, instrumental in future-proofing technologies, products and services. In BIOMAC RISE 
will be PL owners for BNC applications. RISE Processum will contribute to WP3 in Task 3.4 through the production 
of bacterial nanocellulose (BNC) which will be used for reinforcement of biobased PLA foils. The BNC production 
will be based on previous experience at RISE Processum. Briefly, a bacterial strain isolated at RISE Processum will 
be used in cultivation experiments in pilot bioreactors using a hydrolysate containing fermentable sugars as substrate 
in the stirred tank bioreactors. RISE Processum will also participate in Task 3.6 where hydrolysates produced by 
RISE Processum will be used for the generation of bioresins. Enzymatic hydrolysis of fibre sludge (residual stream 
from pulp and paper industry) will be performed.  Additionally, RISE will be involved in WP2 concerning the 
upgrade of Pilot Lines as well as in WP4 for the characterisation of starting and raw materials and final products in 
terms of their physical, structure and morphological properties.  The test cases related to the work of RISE are 
targeting the food packaging materials and the printed electronics (TeC3, TeC5) . They will support the OITB 
clustering activities at Task 9.2, the administrative and financial project management at task 10.1 and technical 
project management at Task 10.2. As all partners they  will be involved in activities regarding the exploitation and 
dissemination of the BIOMAC ecosystem in the context of WP8 & 9.

internationally. RISE Processum has participated in many research projects and publications, some of which are

4.1.8 Leibniz Institute for Agricultural Engineering and Bioeconomy 
Short Name ATB Type RTD Country DE 
 
http://www.atb-potsdam.de/ 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
The Leibniz Institute for Agricultural Engineering and Bioeconomy is a nationally and internationally operating 
research centre. At the interface of biological and technical systems, the institute follows an interdisciplinary 
approach, combining basic research with a high degree of application orientated research. 
The Institu te’s mission is to develop sustainable and highly innovative technologies for the resource efficient 
utilization of biological systems to produce food, raw materials and energy. Climate change and the incipient 
changes in the structure of agriculture repre sent particular challenges for agricultural engineering research. ATB 
research activities are of interdisciplinary nature and follow a systems approach covering the entire spectrum from 
primary production and consumption of food, feed and non-food biomass including technology assessment. 
Founded in 1992, the ATB is today one of the largest agricultural research institutions in Europe and operates - in 
part as a coordinator - in large national research networks as well as in numerous EU and DFG projects. The  ATB 
has state-of-the-art infrastructure, including special laboratories, large -scale facilities, pilot plants (e.g. pilot plant 
for lactic acid) and experimental facilities as well as the newly established Centre for Technology and Knowledge 
Transfer. 
Role in the Project 
 
PL7 (ATB, DE) Enzymatic Hydrolysis & Microbial Fermentation for SA and LA. 
 
ATB is involved in BIOMAC providing the PL7 of Enzymatic Hydrolysis & Microbial Fermentation for SA and 
LA. Particularly they will work on WP2 for the upgrade of the existing pilot lines as well as on WP3 in Task3.2 for 
Automotive Test Case and Task 3.3 for Agricultural Mulch Films Test Case. Specifically, ATB will develop an 
efficient fermentation process for lactic acid (LA) and succinic acid (SA) through the optimization and elucidation 
of various parameters. Several steps of the entire bioprocess needs to be optimized: (1) Enzymatic hydrolysis - 
depolymerizing biopolymers like starch, cellulose to fermentative sugars glucose (C6) and xylose (C5), by means 
of hydrolytic enzymes; (2) Fermentation metabolizing sugars to LA/SA (3) Separation and purification of 
lactic/succinic acid purification to meet t he standards of commercial applications. A stable continuous process 
improves the entire productivity, online measurement devices to get quicker results of different steps especially for 
DSP will be evaluated. Optimization of fermentation conditions will focus on initial sugar concentration, addition 
of commercial (e.g. yeast extract) and/or crude nutrient supplements. Modelling studies will focus on the evaluation 
of kinetic parameters including the inhibitory effect of by -products and/or impurities to mic robial growth and 
product formation. Fermentation runs will be carried out in batch, fed -batch and continuous fermentation mode in 
order to compare productivity, yield, final LA/SA concentration, cost aspects and environmental criteria. The 
adapted strain(s) may be able to sustain inhibitory conditions during continuous fermentation. ATB will adapt and/or 
develop LA/SA purification considering process scalability, purity/quality, robustness, separation yield and cost -
competitiveness. One criterion should be the comparison with already existing figures related to other fermentation 
feedstock. All the necessary components (filtration, electrodialysis, ion exchange, evaporation etc.) are available on 
bench as well as pilot scale. The optimised process in lab-scale (1-3 L bioreactors) will be scaled up in pilot -scale 
up to 450L bioreactor systems for fermentation. This task will also provide several product samples in certain 
qualities for further processing and useful data for economic and environmental assessment, respectively. Moreover, 
ATB will participate in WP9 to support activities related to the engagement of stakeholders, clients and the wider 
public to BIOMAC Ecosystem.

4.1.9 University of Edinburgh 
Short Name UEdin Type  RTD Country UK 
 
www.ed.ac.uk 
 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
The University of Edinburgh is one of the largest and most successful universities in the UK with an international 
reputation as a centre of academic excellence. Its international character is reflected in its student population, which 
comprises of over 3,800 European students and over 9,500 International students (out of a total population of around 
26,500 students at undergraduate level and 15,300 postgraduate) from over 120 different countries worldwide. It can 
also be found in its truly international st aff and in its joint research and other links with overseas universities, 
institutes, companies and governments.  
The University is the leading research university in Scotland and is amongst the top ten in the United Kingdom. 
Almost all members of staff at the university are research active. Following the announcement of the results of the 
2014 Research Assessment Exercise some 63% of the University’s research activity is in the highest categories (4* 
and 3*), of which one third is recognised as “world -leading”. A total of 1,852 individuals, more than 83% of the 
institution’s academic staff, saw their research assessed across 31 subject areas. The results place the University in 
the top 5 in the UK and number one in Scotland by volume of 4* “world-leading” research. The University is home 
to 35% of Scotland’s 4* research. 
On a European level, traditionally the University has been very successful in participating in European Framework 
Programmes. During the Sixth and Seventh Framework Programmes the University  was involved in over 600 
projects, total award value of approximately €320M, and 308 projects in Horizon 2020 with a value of over €213m. 
This includes 52 ERC grants under FP7 a (with a total value of €88.5m) and 68 ERC grants in Horizon 2020 (19 
Advanced, 18 Consolidator, 4 proof of concept, and 27 Starting) with a total value of over €105m. In addition 83 
projects in Horizon 2020 have been MSCA projects. These consist of: 1 COFUND, which we coordinate; 3 RISE, 
one of which we coordinate; 24 ITNs and 56 Individual fellowships. 
It is the University's stated aim that it wishes as far as possible to conduct its research and development activities on 
a trans-national basis. The pooling of research expertise, equipment and database resources contributes to majo r 
advances in science, technology and medicine worldwide.   
Role in the Project 
 
PL8 (UEdin, UK) Pyrolysis and carbonisation of biomass 
 
UEdin is strongly involved in WP1 with the organisation and operation of the OITB. In WP2 (Tasks 2.1-2.4), UEdin 
will focus on upgrading and optimisation of the pilot-scale thermal processing unit. The work relates tothe feedstock 
flexibility (size, density, shape, etc.) process monitoring and control, and environmental performance (effluent and 
product gas handling), with the aim to enable reliable, efficient and safe processing of a range of materials into 
selected final products, such as porous solid carbons and phenol -rich liquids. In WP3, UEdin will be contribute to 
three tasks, validating performance of the upgraded PL. In Task 3.3, (Test Case 2Agricultural Mulch Films) UEdin 
will  develop and provide biochar materials to be tested and used in agricultural applications as a component of or  
in combination with innovative soil mulch films. In Task 3.5, UEdin will contribute to Test Case 4 : Construction, 
by developing and providing biochar materials to be tested in construction applications. In Task 3.6, UEdin will 
contribute to Test Case 5: Printed Electronics, by developing and providing conductive carbon materials and phenolic 
compounds (from lignin and biomass thermal fractionation) to be used in inks, bio-resins and printable electronics. 
In WP4, UEdin will participate in the Validation Hub Services by providing services to clients and data for modelling 
activities. Further to this, UEdin will contribute to WPs 5-9 in different parallel actions.

Infrastructure & technical equipment 
The UK Biochar Research Centre at the University of Edinburgh offers a unique set of biomass thermal treatment 
facilities for solid carbon and pyrolysis liquid product development. At the core is a pilot -scale plant capable of 
handling up to 50kg/h of biomass, supported by laboratory experimen tal and analytical facilities (MS, TGA -DSC, 
TG-MS, Karl-Fischer titration, GC-MS, …). The unit has been used for fundamental research as well as for product 
development and testing, e.g. in collaboration with a spin-out company Carbogenics Ltd. (www.carbogenics.com), 
as well as large international companies in areas of chemical processing, polymers and packaging. 
As part of the BIOMAC project the pilot scale facility will be upgraded to allow higher feedstock flexi bility (size, 
density, shape, etc.) so that difficult to handle materials, e.g. lignin or nanoparticle containing materials, can be 
processed, advanced process monitoring and control (feedstock composition, product quality, material flows, 
temperature, gas  composition, etc.), improved product recovery and separation (porous carbons, phenolic 
compounds, organic acids, etc.), and improved environmental performance (effluent and product gas handling and 
monitoring). The aim is to enable reliable, efficient and  safe processing of a range of materials into selected final 
products, such as porous solid carbons and phenol-rich liquids.

Dr. Ondřej Mašek (Male) is a Reader in Engineering Systems at UK Biochar Research Centre, 
School of Geosciences, University of Edinburgh (UEd). He is one of the co -founders of the UK 
Biochar Research Centre (UKBRC) where he leads the pyrolysis research group and manages a 
set of unique biochar development and production facilities. OM is working on development of 
processes and technologies for sustainable biomass processing and co -production of biochar, 
energy carriers and bio -chemicals. He also develops new biochar -based or bioc har-containing 
products for environmental and engineering applications. OM has published over 60 peer -
reviewed papers and book chapters on biomass pyrolysis and gasification, biochar production, 
characterisation and utilisation of pyrolysis co -products. He leads UEd’s contribution to H2020 
project GreenCarbon focused on development of biomass -based carbons, their engineering and 
environmental applications, a Newton Fund project with Indonesia focussed on maximising 
efficiency of biomass use in rural communities, a Commonwealth fellowship focussed on biochar 
upgrading, and is a Co -I on a BBSRC project “A Scalable Bio -based Solution to Eliminate 
Cyanotoxins in Drinking Water” where he leads development of biochar for removal of toxins 
from drinking water. He is also the UK representative in COST Action (LignoCOST) CA17128. 
In the BIOMAC project, OM will lead the PL8 activities and engagement with the project 
management, stakeholders and internal as well as external partners. OM is involved in a number 
of projects relating to the development of biochar and its uses in environmental applications in a 
number of countries (UK, Indonesia, Pakistan, Sri Lanka, China, Brazil, Chile) providing 
expertise highly relevant to this proposal.

4.1.10 ASOCIACION DE INVESTIGACION DE MATERIALES PLASTICOS Y CONEXAS 
Short Name AIMPLAS Type  RTD Country ES 
 
 
www.aimplas.net 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
AIMPLAS, Plastic Technology Center located in Valencia, is a private, non-profit Association with more than 600 
associated companies created in 1990. AIMPLAS is formed by +170 highly skilled professional, more than 70% 
with a Masters, Engineering or equivalent degree in Chemistry, polymer engineering,  materials engineering or 
equivalent, including 20 PhD. 
AIMPLAS’ fields of work are related to technological research and development on thermoplastic and thermosetting 
plastic materials & products, its transformation processes and their recyclability and sustainability. AIMPLAS 
generates new knowledge and technologies that can be transferred to companies in order to help them to increase 
their effectiveness and competitiveness. 
AIMPLAS has a broad expertise in the fields of recycling, compatibilization, re active extrusion, biopolymers and 
renewable source materials, special assisted processing technologies and nanocomposites, gained during the last 
years in the frame of EU and national projects. Nowadays, AIMPLAS is involved in more than 27 European projects 
and has participated in 79 projects in FP5, FP6, FP7, LIFE+, CIP -EcoInnovation EU Programmes, among others, 
coordinating 27 of them. At National and Regional levels AIMPLAS participates in around 100 projects yearly. 
AIMPLAS develops tailored R&D projects to meet the needs of companies in the packaging and food sector. Some 
of the investigation lines which stand out in packaging sector are: 
 
✓ Development of biodegradable and bio-based materials 
✓ Improved properties: antimicrobial, barrier properties, functional barriers 
✓ Processing of biodegradable materials: extrusion, foaming, injection 
✓ Active packaging 
 
AIMPLAS commitment to corporate social responsibility policies. In AIMPLAS, the Plastics Technology Centre, 
we develop solutions for the present and we research to contribute to the progress. We pre -empt the needs of the 
industry and the society. For that purpose, one of the premises for the success of our project is the sustainable 
development and the well -being of individuals, an end to w hich we contribute through the performance of our 
activity and our Corporate Social Responsibility (CSR). 
AIMPLAS’ strategy on CSR is based on the commitment to the Global Compact of the United Nations, to which we 
have joined. Regarding equality, a plan has been implemented to allow obtaining an equality seal from the Regional 
Government of Valencia. At the same time, we have implemented a flexibility policy in the work calendar to make 
possible the conciliation of work and family life and we have develope d actions aimed at promoting healthy habits 
among employees. 
For years now, we are committed to social development through its implementation with the support of AIMPLAS 
Board of Directors. 
Role in the Project 
 
PL11 (AIMP, ES) Reactive extrusion (REX) for PLA and PLA copolymer based nanocomposites. 
 
AIMPLAS will lead the PL11, the synthesis of PLA by Reactive extrusion from lactide. First, LA obtained in PL7 
will be converted to Lactide by oligomerization of LA followed by depolymerization, dimeri zation and final 
purification. Then, PLA will be obtained in by Ring Opening Polymerization of Lactide by means of the Reactive 
extrusion process. The reaction kinetics, formulation and suitable molecular weight will be first studied in a 
HAAKE™ MiniLab extruder or in a Brabender Plastic order. Finally, the reactive extrusion will be upscaled to pilot 
plant in a co-rotating twin screw extruder line where the final process parameters (screw and extruder configuration, 
temperature profile, throughput and residence time) will be set up. A simulation software will be used to design and 
optimize the reactive process. The obtained polymers will be characterized to determine their molecular weight, 
mechanical, thermal and rheological properties.  PL11 will interact with other BIOMAC’s PLs by the introduction 
of obtained nanoparticles in the reactive extrusion of PLA to improve material’s properties with the objective to 
meet the requirements in Test Case: Food packaging as well as in Test Case 2: Agricultural Mulch Films (Task 3.4 
and 3.3 accordingly). AIMPLAS will also be involved in Task 4.2 concerning the characterization of materials and 

DT-NMBP-04-2020    
 
[BIOMAC]   [35 of 115] 
products. Finally, they will also support LCA and LCC activities (WP6) and will contribute to project dissemination 
activities (WP9).

Infrastructure & technical equipment 
AIMPLAS has more than 9,000 m2 of cutting -edge facilities located in Paterna (Valencia), Spain. About 4000 m2 
are dedicated to laboratories, and 5000m2 are distributed among more than 20 pilot plants with different processes 
for plastic processing. The plants’ equipment covers all the plastic transformation processes, both thermoplastics and 
thermosetting, or composites. 
Among all technical equipment available in AIMPLAS, the most interesting for the present project are listed below: 
• Equipment to carry out mechanical, thermal, rheological and physical tests for material characterization, 
accredited according EN/ISO standards. 
• Rheometer, optical and electronic microscopy, DMA, DSC, TGA, FT-IR, Raman Spectrometer, SEC. 
• Kilo laboratory for the synthesis of poly mers from multigrams to kilograms level, process optimization; 
reaction time, temperature, pressure, design of catalyst system, purification, etc. The kilolab is equipped 
with glass jacketed reactors from 0.1 to 50L able to reach temperatures of 190ºC, ste el reactors of 0.1, 0.5 
and 10L steel reactors able to reach temperatures up to 250ºC and pressures from 30 to 200bar. Moreover, 
high volume Buchi rotavapor of 20L capacity and high capacity crystallization/filtration systems. Other 
auxiliary equipment as vertical stirrers for viscous polymers, vacuum pumps, water traps, nitrogen line and 
vacuum oven are currently available. 
• HAAKE™ MiniLab II Micro Compounder and Brabender Plasticorder torque rheometer, which are ideal to 
design, study and optimize the reac tive extrusion process at laboratory scale (8 to 50g per batch), when 
expensive materials or only small amounts of raw materials are available: nano -composites, new bio -
polymers or pharmaceuticals.

• Four pilot lines with Twin-screw co-rotating extruders with L/D from 25 to 56, and screw diameter from 16 
to 27mm, equipped with gravimetric loss -in-weight feeders for solids (polymers, monomers, fillers, 
additives) and liquids (plasticizers, monomers and additives). The pilot lines are completed with vacuum 
pums and traps to extract volatiles and residual monomers, air cooled belt conveyor, water bath and strand 
pelletizer, and underwater pelletizer for polymer granulation. 
• Flat sheet extrusion and blown film extrusion for monolayer and multilayer co-extrusion of polymers up to

4.1.11 Fraunhofer-Gesellschaft zur Förderung der angewandten Forschung e.V., Fraunhofer Instiute for 
Wood Research – Wilhelm-Klauditz-Institut (WKI) 
Short Name FH-WKI Type  RTD Country DE 
 
 
https://www.fraunhofer.de/ 
 https://www.wki.fraunhofer.de/ 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
Fraunhofer is Europe’s leading application-oriented research organization. Our research efforts are geared entirely 
to people’s needs: health, security, communication, energy and the environment. As a result, the work undertaken 
by our researchers and developers has a significant impact on people’s lives. We are creative. We shape technology. 
We design products. We improve methods and techniques. We open up new vistas. In short, we forge the future. 
The research activities of the Fraunhofer -Gesellschaft are conducted by 74 institutes and research institutions at 
locations throughout Germany. International collaboration with outstanding research partners and companies from 
around the world brings Fraunhofer into direct contact with the key regions that drive scientific progress and 
economic development. 
The Fraunhofer WKI is one of the 74 research institutes within the Fraunhofer Society. The research and 
development activities of the WKI serve to achieve a better utilization of the raw material wood and other 
renewable raw materials as well as an increase in the quality of the products produced therefrom. As an accredited 
testing body, the Fraunhofer WKI undertakes tasks concerning material testing and quality monitoring. It assesses 
cases of damage and provides advice regarding damage restoration. 
The Department of Surface Technology at the Fraunhofer WKI develops paints and adhesives on the basis of 
vegetable oils, sugars, lignin and waste materials. The research focusses on the entire value chain of wood coatings 
and adhesion, including the synthesis of binders, formulation and application of coatings. Method development of 
weather-related aging processes, standard tests and damage analysis complete the profile.  
Role in the Project 
 
PL12 (FH-WKI, DE) Resins Pilot Line 
 
For BIOMAC Project the Fraunhofer WKI will bring in their expertise in the synthesis of bio -based polyols, 
polyester and polyurethane resins that can be used as prepolymer or polymer resins for thermosetting and UV -
curing materials. Applications are UV-curing coatings, UV-curing additive manufacturing or thermally curing fibre 
reinforced composites. In detail this involves the synthesis of bio -based UV -curing materials for additive 
manufacturing for automotive applications in Task 3.2. The focus will be placed on materials wi th high heat 
deflection temperature, low weight and high ductility. Further to this, bio-based polymer resins that can be used as 
binders for printed electronics will be developed (Task 3.6). In addition to the polymer resins synthesis, formulation 
of the UV-curing materials will be conducted in order to develop materials that can be used as UV -curing AM-
materials. Moreover, FH-WKI will support activities related to the upgrade of the existing pilot lines (WP2). The 
Fraunhofer WKI has the possibility to opt imize resins on lab scale (up to 1 kg) and small technical reactor scale 
(up to 4 kg). The latter allows for an easy transfer of the conditions to a larger technical scale at other facilities. 
Finally, FH-WKI will participate in WP9 to support activities r elated to the engagement of stakeholders, clients 
and the wider public to BIOMAC Ecosystem.

Infrastructure & technical equipment 
The Department of Surface Technology at the Fraunhofer WKI offers a fully equipped synthesis and analytical 
laboratory for R+D activities of polymer resins, such as polyesters, polyurethanes, PU -dispersions and other 
polymer dispersions. Synthesis can be conducted on lab scale (up to 2 kg) and in a small side double wall reactor 
(see pictures below). The latter allows small scale up to 4 kg under similar conditions used in industrial production 
processes. In addition, coatings and resin formulations can be executed in our facilities . For the analysis of the 
polymer resins and the formulated products the following equipment is available at the WKI: GPC, FTIR, HPLC, 
rotational viscometer, particle size determination. Coatings can be applied by simple application by means of a 
squeegee, spray coating, 3D-printing. Furthermore, UV-curing of coatings is possible. The dried/cured polymer 
samples can be analyzed by tensile test, Charpy-test, artificial and natural weathering. 
 
The Fraunhofer WKI therefore can provide full service for companies interested in developing new polymer resins 
for coating, printing ink and additive manufacturing applications.

2013 he works as scientist at the Fraunhofer WKI in Braunschweig. His research interests 
involve bio-based polymers and polymer resins, UV-curing polymers for inks and materials for 
additive manufacturing, and material use of bio-based side-products.

4.1.12 Creative Nano PC 
Short Name Cnano Type  SME Country GR 
 
www.creativenano.gr 
 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
Creative Nano (Cnano) is a research and commercialization SME focusing on technological product-based solutions 
specialized in the field of nanotechnology. The company was founded in 2013 (as Artia Nanoengineering and 
Consulting) and has reached its final form after a merging in summer of 2018. Cnano’s team consists of MSc and 
PhD level scientists and engineers with extensive experience on working and collaborating with companies, research 
institutes and universities across Europe to solve technical impasses and create innovations that establish a 
competitive advantage for its clients. Cnano specializes in the field of development, production, sales and application 
of high performance composite protective coatings. Our technical know-how lies in the manufacturing, deposition, 
dispersion, upgrading and processing of in-organic nano- and microparticles into functional coatings. The company 
aims to  commercialize coating materials and acquire research and development projects through corporate 
collaborations producing tailor -made solutions for its customers. With the help of nanotechnology Cnano is 
developing consumer -based solutions in synthesis, pr ocessing and manufacturing of nanomaterials, composite 
nanocoatings, nanoparticles, hybrid systems and liquid systems. Cnano develops products with enhanced properties 
such as corrosion resistance, high transparency, water repellence, self -cleaning, anti -finger-print, abrasion -
resistance, temperature resistance, anti-delamination and photocatalytic. 
Role in the Project 
 
PL4 (Cnano, GR) US assisted PL reactor for the production of NL 
 
Cnano is specialized and works in the field of development, production, sales and application of nanomaterials, high 
performance and advanced surface modifying processes. In BIOMAC project Cnano will provide PL4 related to the 
ultrasound-assisted treatment of lignocellulosic biomass for the production of nano lignin particles.  Cnano will be 
involved in WP2 where the upgrade of existing Pilot Lines is planned. In close collaboration with PoliMi will work 
on activities related to the process optimization of the US-assisted treatment of lignocellulosic biomass as well as to 
the upgrading and upscaling of the ultrasound-assisted apparatus. In WP3 they will participate in Task 3.3,Test case 
2: Agricultural Mulch Films. PL4 of Cnano will receive the lignin to produce through a US process nanolignin that 
will be incorporated in the biopolymers formulation stage of pellets in order to provide antioxidant properties to  
mulch films. Moreover, they will provide NL at Task 3.4, Test Case 3 : Food Packaging, for the production of 
packaging films based on bio -based PLA film reinforced with  NL. Additionally, Cn will also contribute in WP9 
related to Dissemination, Communication and Clustering activities in order to disseminate BIOMAC Ecosystem  to 
targeted audiences.

Infrastructure & technical equipment 
Cnano has its own manufacturing facilities in Athens with a state -of-the-art equipped laboratory (microscopes, 
spectrometers), along with the semi -industrial mixing reactor (5 tanks with effective volume of 80 L per tank) for 
development and characterizati ons of nano -enabled paints. Cnano has extensive experience on the production of 
nano-enabled paint formulations with antimicrobial and photocatalytic activities.  
 
 
Semi-industrial mixing reactor 
 
At the same time, Creative Nano provides technical support for material characterization and data analysis and 
processing, based on existing standards, for the characterization of nanomaterials, according to quality and safety  
control procedures. In particular, Creative Nano performs characterizations on chemical composition, solubility, etc.,  
as well as determining functional surface properties, shape, stability, wettability, adsorption potential, concentration,  
adhesion, etc. In addition, Creative Nano  has great expertise in determining mechanical properties, tribology and  
surface features, ensuring functional real -time evaluation. Techniques: Electrochemical techniques  
[(photo)voltammetry, photocurrent spectroscopy, chrono-amperometry, optical characterization methods (reflection  
/absorption spectroscopy of solid films, photoreflectance), UV -Vis spectroscopy, mechanical properties of solid  
surfaces (micro -hardness), thermal treatment, chemical and mechanical treatments of solid surfaces. Laboratory  
infrastructure

4.1.13 Instituto Tecnológico del Embalaje, Transporte y Logística 
Short Name ITENE Type  RTD Country SP 
 
www.itene.com  
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
ITENE is the specialist Technological Centre in R&D in packaging, logistics, transport and mobility. Its mission is to 
generate scientific and technological knowledge and adding value to companies through the implementation of R+D+I 
in these areas. ITENE provides business solutions with an integrated view of the supply chain, from raw materials, 
design and development of packaging and packaging systems, optimisation of the movement and distribution of goods, 
until the products reach the consumer and are ultimately managed as residues, all within a framework of sustainable 
performance. The centre has advanced f acilities and a multidisciplinary team of researchers and technicians with 
proven and constantly evolving technologies for novel solutions. 
ITENE was founded in 1994 and currently employs 153 persons. Located in Valencia, Spain, the centre has 7,105m2 
of facilities covering laboratories and experimentation infrastructures equipped with the most modern technology. 
ITENE research area covers: 
• New Advanced Materials (Development strategies to obtain new packaging materials with better properties) 
• Functional surfaces and Intelligent Packaging.  
• Food safety and Active Packaging (Materials that release active substances from the packaging or absorb 
undesirable substances from the product to prolong the shelf life)   
• Packaging Technologies (vacuum, modified atmosphere) 
• Packaging Engineering (Transport simulation technologies) 
• Sustainability (Waste valorisation, LCA, LCC, Carbon Footprint) 
• Transport and Logistics (route optimization, distribution modelling, urban mobility) 
• Electronics, Robotics and Industry 4.0 
ITENE has participated in 39 projects from FP6 and FP7 and is involved in 25 H2020 projects (most of them under 
execution). 
The advanced materials department provides expertise and new facilities to support the study and development of new 
materials in the nanometer range, including the design, synthesis and application of nanomaterials in relevant industrial 
sectors. This group has relevant experience in the development of biocoating, including Synthesis and characterization 
of bio -based materials, formula tion and production of new bio -plastics solutions with advanced properties and 
advanced compounding for high performance and cost -efficient bio-based plastics. Our Food safety department has 
relevant experincie on food Contact issues (participating in technical committees, both Spanish and European, related 
to Food Contact Materials Regulations). 
Role in the Project 
 
PL13 (ITE, ES) Mechanical treatment to produce NFC and / or CNC 
PL14 (ITE, ES) Coating Formulation PL 
 
ITENE will be leading the deployment and demonstration of its own pilot lines (PL13 &PL14) to produce NFC and/or 
CNC, which would be functionalized according to the needs of its final use, and to formulate nano-based coatings and 
inks. ITENE will be also s upporting the Test Cases on Agriculture mulch film (TC2), Food packaging (TC3), and 
Printed electronics (TC5) under Tasks 3.3, 3.4, and 3.5 accordingly. In WP2 ITENE will be involved in the process 
monitoring and optimization of Pilot Lines. as Additionally, in WP4 ITENE is leading the characterization task of 
materials and products. Finally, ITENE will participate in general tasks regarding communication, dissemination, and 
exploitation issues.

Infrastructure & technical equipment 
ITENE uses 7,000 square metres of its installations as laboratories and experimentation facilities, equipped with the 
latest technology for research and testing, and product and services development. R&D activities are carried out in the 
following laboratories: Nano Additives and Nano Clay Pilot Plant, Nano Safety Laboratory, Chemical Laboratory, , 
Packaging Manufacturing Pilot Plant, Packaging Pilot Plant, Microbiology Laboratory, Packaging Evaluation 
Laboratory, Transport Simulation Centre, RFID Pilot Plant, and Ink formulation laboratory. 
Main equipment to be used in the project are described next: 
 
• 20 L Digestor allows the modification of the nanocellulose fibers which will be used as reinforcement in 
coating and ink. This equipment contains: Temperature control, Stirring system, 20 L of capacity, 
Production: 100 g/day  
• Filtration system allows for small-scale, which work which works on batch. This filtration system has a 
capacity of 5 L/batch. 
• 150 L Digestor allows the modification of the nanocellulose fibers for big-scale which will be used as 
reinforcement in coating and ink. This equipment contains:  Temperature control,  Stirring system, 150 L of 
capacity, Production: 200-1000 g/day  
• Grinder: used to disintegrate the cellulosic pulp through a mechanical process to obtain nanocellulose fibers. 
Production capability of the 1kg/day. 
• Spray-drier lab scale for drying of nanocellulose on a laboratory scale. Production: 5-10 g/day 
• Spray-drier pilot scale Spray-drier lab scale allows drying of nanocellulose on a laboratory scale. 
Production: 50-55 g/day 
• 20 L Acid Digestor allows the production of the nanocrystal of cellulose from different cellulosic pulp. To 
obtain the nanocrystals of cellulose a acid process with sulfuric acid will be used. 
• Ultraturrax IKA T25 High-performance dispersion instrument for volumes from 1 to 2000 ml (H2O) with 
digital speed display

CHARACTERIZATION OF NANOCELLULOSE: 
 
• Turbidimeter to determine of the turbidity of nanocellulose suspensions. This parameter is an important 
parameter to determinate the Quality Index of the nanocellulose.  
• Sheet former Rapid Köthen allows to obtain nanopapers from the different nanocellulose, which will be 
measured on the Universal testing machine to determinate the Young’s Module. 
• Centrifugal is needed to evaluate the performance of nanofibrillation, which is the percentage of fibers that 
have a nanometric size. 
• Optical microscope is used to determinate the macroscopic side of the fibers. This parameter is the last to 
determinate the Quality Index of nanocellulose. 
• Moisture analyser allows to determinate the sold content that a nanocellulose suspension has.

4.1.14 ASOCIACIÒN DE INVESTIGACIÓN METALÚRGICA DEL NOROESTE 
Short Name AIMEN Type  RTD Country ES 
 
 
www.aimen.es 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
AIMEN Technology Centre is a Non -Profit Innovation and Technology Centre, that was set up in 1967, highly 
specialized in materials and in advanced manufacturing technologies applied to high performance materials development 
and processing, robotics and automation. It provides technological support to more than 500 companies dedicated to 
industrial or commercial activity in the fields of Automotive, Aeronautics, Shipbuilding, Metal - Mechanical, Wind 
Energy, Metallurgy, Chemical and Building. AIMEN promotes and undertakes research, as well as improves design, 
simulation and manufacturing techno logies. AIMEN's Research and Development office has been registered as a 
Technology Transfer Office since April, 2002 by the Inter-ministry Commission for Science and Technology, under the 
Number 166, and registered as a Centre of Innovation and Technology  (CIT) under number 38 in the Registry of the 
Inter-ministry Commission for Science and Technology. 
 
AIMEN facilities, 9.000 m2 of technological and scientific infrastructure 
Located in the Northwest of Spain (headquarters, Error! Reference source not found. ) with office also in Madrid, 
Basque Country and Sevilla, AIMEN is a highly professionalized organisation, with more than 240 employees 
specialised in the fields of Materials Science, Welding, Manufacturing Process Engineering, Robotics and Control 
Engineering, Testing, and Laser Processing. Its mission is to improve the competitiveness and the technological know-
how of the manufacturing industry through the following activities: (i) R&D projects, (ii) Technology forecasting, (iii) 
Acquisition and development of emergent technologies, (iv) Promotion of technological innovation insi de the 
companies. Around 2/3 of all R&D projects are in collaboration with the industry, with the objective of providing new 
technological solutions in the medium term. AIMEN is aware of the importance of quality together with protecting the 
environment, safety of people, security information and R&D&I management. 
The R&D activity in AIMEN can be grouped into the following research fields: 
- High Performance Materials: Multimaterial systems, hybrid materials, processing of polymeric matrix composites 
(thermoplastic and thermosetting), thermoplastic welding, coatings technologies, polymer compounding, embedded 
control systems for polymer manufacturing. 
- Laser Based Manufacturing: additive manufacturing, laser assisted processing, high quality laser productio n, high 
power / high throughput laser processing, laser surface activation of polymers and fibres. 
- High Precision Manufacturing: production of functional surfaces, 3D micropart production, microfabrication and 
micro-manufacturing systems. 
- Robotics: mobile and collaborative manipulators, robotics for transport and logistics, mechatronics. 
- Smart Manufacturing: advanced assembly and disassembly technologies, robotics and flexible automation, embedded 
monitoring and control. 
- Environmental technologies: waste management, water quality and treatment, wetlands, life cycle.management, 
environmental monitoring 
AIMEN has experience in R&D collaborative projects as a coordinator of several National and European projects 
It has been involved in the design, production and monitoring of different polymeric matrix composites, the automation, 
control and robotizing of different welding, and with the development of new manufacturing processes of thermoplastic 
composites. 
AIMEN has active presence in the main European and National technology platforms and initiatives related with 
materials and manufacturing technologies, as for example the EFFRA (related to Factories of the Future PPP), 
EuRobotics (linked to SPARC PPP) and EU Platforms like SUSCHEM, EuMAT, ManuFUTURE or  Photonics21.
