AIMEN has an active role in these initiatives, and has contributed to the definition of R&D priorities at national and 
European level, including the RIS3-Galicia strategy. AIMEN is also present in other national and international expert 
panels, consulting committees, groups and societies, like the International Institute of Welding, EARTO, the European 
Laser Institute ELI, sectorial industry clusters (automotive, shipbuilding, metalworking), as well as in EPIC (European 
Photonics Industry Cluster) and SECPhO (Southern European Cluster in Photonics and Optics 
Role in the Project 
 
PL15 (AIMEN, ES) Additive manufacturing (AM) 
 
Within BIOMAC, the technical work to be developed by AIMEN will be the setup of a Pilot Line providing end-users 
with 3D printing technologies to validate the new bio/nano -based materials into new products. Two of the Additive 
Manufacturing (AM) available technologies to be used during the project, FDM and photopolymerization AM, will 
cover a wide range of materials: both thermoplastics (FDM) and UV curable thermosets (photopolymerization AM). 
The activities will encompass the AM processability tests of the new bio-based polymers with 3D printing technologies 
to validate the full value chain, including the shaping of the material in the processing format (e.g. filaments for FDM). 
AIMEN will lead PL15: Additive Manufacturing, thus participating in WP2: Upgrade  Pilot Lines by adapting a 
robotized additive manufacturing cell for biopo lymers and large parts manufacturing including the design of path 
planning strategies, Moreover, they will be involved in WP3 mainly in Tasks 3.1, 3.2 and 3.3, related with the 
manufacturing of the Test Case 1: Automotive and Test Case 4: Construction. AIM EN in collaboration with other 
partners will participate in WP4: Validation Hub Services. AIMEN will develop Additive Manufacturing services in 
WP7: Open call & Intra Test Cases. Finally, they will also provide the information needed from the pilot plant a nd 
additive manufacturing process to the partners leading the transversal activities as standardization and regulatory aspects 
or Life Cycle Assessment (LCA), Exploitation, and Business Plan.

Infrastructure & technical equipment 
Advanced Materials Unit covers different materials such as metal, polymers, metal matrix composite, polymer matrix 
composite, adhesives and resins. Related with composites manufacturing, AIMEN has the following equipment: 
 
Composite & Polymer manufacturing and processing technologies, including Additive Manufacturing – FFF 
(fused filament fabrication) facilities: 
• Filament manufacturing: double screw sigma mixer (45cm3), double screw extruder (200Nm, 450ºC), coating heads 
and nozzles, cooling bath and filament winder. Maximum torque: 200Nm; Maximum speed: 200 min-1; Maximum 
temperature: 450°C 
• 3D printing: A2V4 printing machine (3nt  r) and Ultimaker 2+. Materials: ABS, PA, PEI, PEEK, biomaterials and 
others, including carbon fibre and metallic, wood, and other charges.  
• Development and/or adaptation of FFF printing heads in-house, including the composite materials printing. 
• Robotized printing solutions for large-volume 3D printing (based on robotic arms from ABB, FANUC). 
• Automated composite layering (ATL): Thermoplastic tapes, thermosetting prepregs and dry fibre.

Universal testing machines at AIMEN facilities 
 
LASER equipment: 
The Laser Processing Centre of AIMEN is the largest laser industrial applications centre in Spain, constituting the 
national reference centre for this technology. It provides facilities and expertise for process development and validation 
in support of the manufacturing industry. These facilities enable users to make an informed assessment on the 
applicability of altern ative laser procedures. The facilities are also used to make prototype components and small 
production runs, where the use of specialized equipment is required. In this regard, AIMEN owns several 
micromanufacturing laser sources on 3 or 5 axis precision motion systems; pulsed lasers (femtosecond, picosecond, or 
nanosecond range), with UV, green or IR wavelength; continuous wave single mode fibre lasers (1.5kW); a continuous 
wave disk laser (16kW): 
• Multiple pulsed lasers from femto to nanoseconds. 
• 1070 nm fibre lasers from 400 W to 8 kW. 
• Four and five axis micro and nanopositioners from Newport and Aerotech, with precision air bearing servo 
stages, Newson galvo heads, high numerical aperture optics, integrated range-finder enabled surface scanner.  
• CAD/CAM based development tools for micromanufacturing equipment offline programming. 
• Process monitoring instrumentation: including Photron high speed (100 kfps) camera, Ocean Optics 
spectrometer, PhotonFocus high dynamic range scientific camera, NIT high speed infrared matrix.

4.1.15 POLITECNICO DI MILANO 
Short Name POLIMI Type  RTD Country IT 
 
https://www.polimi.it/en 
 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
With approximately 40,000 students and approximately 1,500 faculty members, Politecnico di Milano (POLIMI) is 
the largest university in Italy for Engineering, Architecture and Industrial Design and it is ranked as one of the 
most outstanding European and global universities in thes e fields (QS World Ranking 2020: 149 th “Global”; 20th 
“Engineering and Technology”; 7th “Architecture”; 6th “Art & Design”). The university has seven campuses located 
in Milan and in other nearby Italian cities. It is organised in 12 Departments, devoted t o research and in 4 Schools, 
devoted to education. Thanks to a strong internationalization policy, many programmes are entirely taught in English, 
thus attracting an ever -increasing number of talented international students, who form a diverse community fr om 
more than 100 countries. POLIMI is member of IDEA League, a strategic alliance among five leading European 
universities of technology that aims to educate a new generation of Engineers with extra -curricular activities for 
selected, highly talented students. 
The POLIMI unit will mainly operate in the Department of Chemistry, Materials and Chemical Engineering 
“Giulio Natta” (www.cmic.polimi.it/en) through the Laboratory of Chemistry and Characterization of Innovative 
Polymers (ChIPlab, http://chiplab.chem.polimi.it). The research unit possesses a strong long -lasting experience in 
the field of polymer and composite science, macromolecular chemistry and materials characterization, physical 
chemistry of surfaces and interfaces, fluorinated polymers and rheolo gy. More specifically, the ChIPlab research 
unit is currently particularly interested in the design, development and characterization of polymeric and composite 
materials for sustainability. The ChIPlab research unit is fully equipped with an extensive ran ge of facilities for 
the synthesis, characterization, processing and testing of polymeric and composite materials that will be fully 
exploited during the project. 
Role in the Project 
PoliMi will provide its contribution in WP2 : Upgrade of Pilot Lines by directly supporting the activities of C nano 
related to the process optimization of the ultrasound -assisted treatment of lignocellulosic biomass and to the 
upgrading and upscaling of the ultrasound-assisted apparatus (PL4). PoliMi will also be involved in WP3 to support 
the activities related to the Test Case 2: Agricultural Mulch Films (Task 3.3) and Test Case 3: Food Packaging (Task 
3.4), providing know how  in the preparation and exploit ation of lignin -based nanoparticles and lignin -based 
polymeric materials. PoliMi will be engaged in WP4, leading the activities in T4.2 related to the characterization 
and validation (i.e., chemical, physical, mechanical and functional performance) of the novel nano-enabled bio-based 
materials exiting the PLs described in WP2 and feeding the Te st Cases addressed in WP3,  utilizing advanced 
characterization techniques. Further to this, PoliMi will lead the action to secure the circular perspective of the 
developments of BIOMAC (Task 6.2 Circular Economy, recycling and EoL management) PoliMi will also 
contribute to WP9: Dissemination, Communication and Clustering with publication of project  results in scientific 
journals and with communication activities to tar geted audiences (conferences, exhibitions, stakeholders), in close 
collaboration with EUBIA.

4.1.16 Danish Teknologisk Institut 
Short Name DTI Type  RTD Country DK 
  
 
https://www.dti.dk/ 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
DTI is the largest technological service provider in Denmark and one of the biggest in northern Europe. Founded 
over 100 years ago, the institute's core business lies in providing technological services to industry, especially 
SMEs. SMEs constitute over 90% of DTI's client base with over 14,000 assignments annually to this sector. The 
institute's expertise is divided into eight divisions c overing building and construction, materials, life sciences, 
industrial management, production technology, energy & climate, meat research and technologies and agriculture. 
These together contain some 33 specialist competence centres with over 22 accredite d laboratories providing 
testing and certification services. The institute is recognized as the leading training and educational institution with 
focus on industry in Denmark and abroad. DTI also advises SMEs in the electronics sector on new business 
development opportunities and assists in the transfer of new technologies. 
Within the production division the Centre for Nano Production and Micro Analysis (N&M) works within the 
commercialization of nanotechnologies. N&M’s conducts commercial surveys annually for over 200 different 
companies with nano characterization and micro machining and is ISO17025 certified.  On top of this, N&M is 
involved in several national and European projects focused on development and production of nanomaterials for 
nano-catalyst and printed electronics applications as well as digital production technologies and energy systems.  
The nano-ink section of N&M is currently working with development of nano Ag and nano Cu materials, ink 
formulation as well as digital production using ink-jet printing.     
Role in the Project 
 
PL16 (DTI, DK) Printed electronics. 
 
DTI will provide PL16 Printed Electronics to develop embed stretchable conductive layers into textiles (sock with 
integrated conductors) using a bio-based stretchable substrate ink and adhesives using printed electronic processes 
for Test Case 5 (Task 3.6) in collaboration with OHMATEX. Moreover, DTI will support activities related to 
inline monitoring and AI of PLs as well as process control and optimization of PLs (Tasks 2.2, 2.3, 2.4). In WP4 
DTI will be involved in workflow design and preparatory validation related to the 5 Test Cases (Task 4.1) as well 
as in the characterization of all the nano -enabled bio-based materials exiting the PLs and the components and 
structures resulting from the Test Cases. Finally, DTI will contribute to activities regarding the dissemination and 
exploitation activities of the BIOMAC Ecosystem.

Description of organization 
Nanotypos is a private start -up company founded in 2012 and located in Thessaloniki (Greece). Nanotypos is a

products that are realized by means of roll -to-roll nanoimprint lithography processes. Nanotypos develops imprint 
based processes based on core expertise in optical devices, photonic applications, biotechnology, energy harvesting 
and organic electronic applications. 
Role in the Project 
 
PL17 (NNT, GR) R2R Nanopatterning and thermoforming. 
 
NNT is a high tech SME pioneering research and technology whose mission is to create, develop, and commercialize 
products such as nanomaterials transferring novel ideas and prototype devices. NNT will contribute to the production 
and replication of large -area micro/nanostructured surfaces with enhanced surface properties. Furthermore, NNT 
will be responsible for the integration of two manufacturing lines in a non -conventional open pilot line, which will 
allow the upscaling of tailored micro/nano -enabled textured polymer film surfaces. (Pilot Line 17: R2R 
Nanopatterning and thermoforming). They will have a strong involvement in Test Case 3 leading by EVERSIA for 
the development of novel custom -configured packaging films based on bio -based PLA film reinforced with BNC 
and NL (Task 3.4) The target is to perform excellent replication, overcoming the current state of the art limitation, 
offering a novel manufacturing process to the EU packaging industry. NNT will al so contribute to the exploitation 
and dissemination of this result through its double role as pilot operator and R&D provider in the mentioned business 
case of the pilot line.

4.1.18 OPTIMIZACIÓN ORIENTADA A LA SOSTENIBILIDAD S.L. 
Short Name IDE Type  SME Country ES 
 
http://www.idener.es 
 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
IDENER is a research SME that investigates in the multidisciplinary field of Computational Science and its 
application to the optimization of systems and processes in key areas: Industrial Technologies; ICTs; Biotechnology; 
Energy; and Resource and Raw Materials Efficiency. 
The company has extensive experience in national and European research and is currently participating in up to 
eleven H2020 projects and three nationally funded projects. Besides, the company par ticipates in major European 
research communities, such as Bio -based Industries (BIC), SPIRE, BIOPLAT, PLANETIC and The European 
Materials Modelling Council (EMMC). 
The Biotech area develops new biotechnology industrial processes for the production of (new)  products from 
unconventional and sustainable sources. The experimental developments in this area are benefited by the synergy 
with computational tools for process and system modelling and optimization. Thanks to this approach, the required 
number of experimental assays is significantly reduced with the subsequent saving of costs and time. Besides, the 
development of predictive models will pave the scale- up of the developed processes. The final result is a high added 
value that sharpens the competitive edge of complex systems by providing improvements in performance and cost-
effectiveness. To that end, IDENER integrates concepts from four interrelated and complementary areas: 
Mathematical Modelling and Simulation; Multidisciplinary Design Optimization; Cont rol Engineering; and 
Software Engineering. The main work lines in the area: (1) Metabolic engineering, (2) Process design and 
development and (3) Process assessment. 
Role in the Project 
IDE is an SME that investigates in the multidisciplinary field of Computational Science and its application to the 
optimization of systems and processes in several areas (Industrial Technologies, ICTs, Biotechnology, Energy, and 
Resource and Raw Materials Efficiency). IDENER will contribute to the optimization and the upgrades of the PLs. 
IDE contributes to the WP2 in Task 2.4 for the optimization of the process in the upgrading of the pilot lines. IDE 
will also be the leader of the WP4 about validation hub services and will be focussed on the validation and predictive 
modeling (Task 4.3). Additionally, IDE will contribute to the dissemination and exploitation strategy of BIOMAC 
Ecosystem.

4.1.20 Universidad De Burgos 
Short Name ICCRAM Type  RTO Country SP 
 
https://www.ubu.es/iccram 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
The University of Burgos (UBU) was founded in 1994 and has assumed its role in the local and regional economy 
and in the larger scientific development responding to market demands (e.g. new grades in accordance to the 
needs of the labor market) and developing wide research networks (e.g. in tegrated research between the 
university, the private sector, public institutions, and civil society organizations). According to the ranking of 
normalized impact on research production elaborated by the CyD (Foundation for Knowledge and Development, 
2011), the University of Burgos holds the 13th position among Spanish Universities with a 1.22 impact index. 
Likewise, according to SCImago Institutions Ranking (SIR 2012), the University of Burgos holds the ES.R 105 
with a Q1 of 55.8 and Excellence Rate of 13. 7, being leader among regional universities. UBU has 67 research 
groups classified in five main research fields: Sciences, Social sciences, Engineering -Construction, Humanities 
and Health sciences. These Research groups have a consolidated prestige not onl y at national but also at 
international level with a relevant number of publications in the best research journals. Under this structure, two 
interdisciplinary groups of the University of Burgos are joining the BIOMAC project: International Research 
Center in Critical Raw Materials for Advanced Industrial Technologies (ICCRAM) and Analysis and Modelling 
of Materials Group (AdF).  
ICCRAM is a part of the Science and Technology Park, integrated by ICCRAM, the Research Center in Food 
Biotechnology (CIBA), the Center for Innovation and Research in Industrial Technology (CITI), as well as a new 
experimental facility in Applied Nanotechnology, and Nano/Toxicity. ICCRAM was born in 2014 conceived to 
integrate within its structure an "intrinsic path into innovation", and it is supported by an industrial board of more 
than 26 industries, SMEs and clusters. ICCRAM is a leading actor in international organizations as PROMETIA, 
the European Innovation Partnership (EIP) on Raw Materials, the Nanosafety Cluster or the International 
Association of Nanotechnology Industries. 
ICCRAM integrates different researching activities in four principal lines: Synth esis of nanomaterials, 
Computational simulation, Nanosafety and Sustainability. From these lines, ICCRAM approaches different topics 
of interest at European level such as definition of recovery, recycling and replacement strategies for critical raw 
materials, application of circular economy principles for new materials design, evaluation of new materials to 
control their environmental, health and safety aspects and biotechnology technologies for industrial, health and 
environmental applications. In this the matic areas, ICCRAM is participating in H2020 projects (MSCA -RISE, 
MSCA-ITN, MSCA -IF, FET -OPEN, NMBP, SC5 and Spreading Excellence) being the coordinator of the 
H2020- MSCA-RISE NANOGENTOOLS, H2020-FET-OPEN ICARUS, H2020 -BIOTEC-08 GREENER and 
H2020-FET-Innnovation Launchpad ICARUS-INAS. 
AdF (Analysis and Modelling of Materials)  research group was established in 2008 in the Department of 
Chemistry of UBU. The group is leaded by Prof. Santiago Aparicio with 10 current members with 
interdisciplinary backgrounds in chemistry, physics and chemical engineering. The research activities  of the 
group are devoted to the development and characterization of new materials for energy and environmental 
applications using combined experimental and theoretical approaches. The group has developed research 
activities in the fields of CO 2 capture and utilization considering many different types of materials. Research 
activities have been funded by national and international agencies and they are developed in collaboration with 
research groups in USA, Qatar, UK, Brazil and South Korea. The group has p ublished more than 100 papers in

Description of organization 
Abis is an independent engineering company that was established in 1994 and specialises in robotics integration, 
production process monitoring, manufacturing and programming industrial control devices. The company has 
experience of programming industrial control devices and computer based process monitoring systems. This includes 
computer control of technological processes and vision systems for quality control. and computer control of 
technological processes and robotics.  Since the beginning Abis has accomplished ove r 600 projects in different 
branches of industry and municipal company. These have been supported through the use of MS Project and their 
trained knowledge of Prince 2 and 6 Sigma methodologies. We rely on modern technologies provided by the world 
most valued companies enriched with Abis tailor -made innovative modules. Excellent training and experience of 
Abis engineers give our customers reliability and high quality of our services. 
 
The main fields of Abis activities are presented below: 
 
Monitoring and production suport: 
 
• SCADA visualization of process lines,  
• data acquisition and reporting using common databases,  
• application on industrial databases solution (Historian),  
• analysis and optimizations of machine work efficiency,  
• administrations of productions orders MES class,  
• delivering and presentation data's through the intranet / internet.  
• quality control systems and statistical data processing, SPC,  
• supplying media accounting solutions,  
Vision quality control: 
• reproducibility with high precision (micrometers scale),  
• detection of splits and scratches in product surface,  
• presents control of multiple objects in package,  
• one and two dimensional barcode reading,  
• recognition of printed texts and stamps,  
• recognition of colors.  
Programming PLC 
• PLC replacement, controls modernization 
• MCC and control cabinets projects and delivery 
• data acquisitions from production lines  
• manufacturing processes and systems,  
• waste water treatment plants,  
• chemical and petrochemical systems,  
• emergency shut down (ESD) installation according to SIL standards,  
• dosing and weighting systems,  
• boiler houses for hot water, steam, fueled by cool, oil and gas.  
Design and implementing robotic and mechatronics solution

Description of organization 
EXELISIS is an engineering-based consulting company located in Athens, Greece. EXE was created by engineers 
and entrepreneurs with extensive experience in business development and innovation specially emphasizing in the 
materials, processes and energy field. EXE IT department, specializes in providing high quality research services 
developing novel computational tools, conducting various types of engineering studies and offering modern 
technological solutions as well as implementing them on multiple applications. Thus, EXELISIS maintains 
numerous ongoing collaborations with stakeholders and municipalities, large industrial enterprises, SMEs, academic 
and public institutions creating a wide, cooperative and beneficial business ecosystem. EXELISIS is providing  its 
services in preparation of action plans for the implementation of vehicle electrification in municipalities establishing 
open innovation environments and creation roadmaps . The current situation and its prospects are depicted on a 
national as well as on a local level, setting specific targets for municipalities in their electrification project and taking 
into account key purpos es. EXELISIS is providing propositions of the project's strategic planning, the financial 
instruments to fund this planning’s i mplementation as well as an outline of the necessary infrastructure to be 
developed. Additionally, EXELISIS is conducting multi actor assessments of the current European and national 
legislative framework surrounding business ecosystems , identifying and pr oposing possible incentives for the 
penetration of in multiple cutting edge market. 
Role in the Project

WP8 and WP9. They will lead the Task 8.1 “Exploitation and Business plan of OITB”. There, new services that 
result from the BIOMAC project will  be identified. A market analysis is to be conducted as well as the LeE to be 
prepared. EXELISIS will perform an economic analysis of the market and the possible opportunities for the 
BIOMAC OITB, evaluating the proposed revenue model’s profitability, defi ning the value proposition, and 
analysing how value is to be created. All this information is to be included in the 3 PEDR deliverables of WP8, 
structured as initial, mid -term updated and final one. Additionally, EXELISIS is to provide support in Task 9.1 : 
Dissemination & Communication activities led by RDC.

4.1.23 European Bioplastics e.V 
Short Name EUBP Type  SME Country DE 
 
 
https://www.european-bioplastics.org 
 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
European Bioplastics is the industry association representing the bioplastics industry in Europe across the entire 
bioplastics value chain. Established over 20 years ago, EUBP now has 70 member companies from across the 
globe. EUBP’s members primarily produce, refine, and distribute bioplastics, i.e. plastics that are bi o-based, 
biodegradable, or both. In addition, biomass feedstock producers, bioplastics converters and compounders, and 
several renowned academic and private research institutions are also members of EUBP. The association’s key 
objectives are: 
✓ to serve as a contact and network platform, as a primary resource for information about the bioplastics 
industry, and as a catalyst for advancing the objectives of the growing bioplastics industry as a whole. 
✓ Coordination of various working groups and product groups focussed on bioplastic -related themes, 
such as the PG Bio-based and PG Biodegradable is also in focus. 
✓ Introduction and monitoring of industry standards (such as EN 13432) and best practices are actively 
supported. 
✓ Contribution to Circular Economy and political processes in Europe by linking to the legislation 
impacting on the bioplastics industry’s ability to fully bring to bear its innovative potential. 
Role in the Project 
EUBP is the largest association and network within the bioplastics industry. It can draw on an extensive close-knit 
network of key personnel in organisations involved in bioplastics research, sourcing, production, distribution, 
consumption, as well as contacts involved in the pertinent political processes, associations, NGOs, and civil society 
organisations. As part of EUBP’s commitment to furthering the goals of the bioplastics industry, acting as catalyst 
for information exchange and distribution, as a trusted source of information, and acting as a convener of some of 
the industry’s key events and working groups is part of EUBP’s primary daily activities. EUBP has departments 
dedicated to policy affairs, member and industry communication and PR, and the te chnical environmental affairs 
department with a focus on bioplastics, whose blend of expertise provides EUBP with the tools to carry out complex 
dissemination activities and reach a vast number of decision makers across the industry. Within BIOMAC Project 
EUBP will undertake the whole administrative, financial and legal issues of the Ecosystem (e.g. marketing, access 
to additional funding, contracts with customers, secretarial and administrative tasks, etc) and will act as the Single 
Entry Point “SEP” of the Ecosystem for the proper representation and operation of the Ecosystem. EUBP will lead 
WP1: Ecosystem organization, tools and procedures and Tasks 1.1, 1.2, 1.4. Moreover,  EUBP’s key task is to 
contribute to aspects of regulatory and policy structure (Task 5.4) for emerging bioplastics with special attention 
to regulations on nanomaterials (nano-safety), guidelines, and procedures. This aim to achieve a smoother market 
implementation by maintaining health working conditions and using existing goods as well as early identification 
of possible conflicts related to advances in BIOMAC, backed by existing tools and contributions to policymaker 
recommendations and standards/guideli nes such as EU Observatory for Nanomaterials (EUON) tools, the EU 
Agency for Safety and Health at Work (EU -OSHA) and OECD -documents. (Task 5.4) . Finally, EUBIA will 
support the project’s dissemination and training activities. EUBP will draw on an extensive  repertoire of 
dissemination and training channels, such as self -organised events, third party events, publications in relevant 
industry and academic publications as well mainstream media, press releases, online and social media channels.  
Relevant publications, products to the project 
• EUBP organises the largest bioplastics industry forum in Europe which can be used for dissemination 
activities. 
• EUBP regularly publishes various background papers, position papers, and similar documents on 
bioplastics and related subjects (https://www.european-bioplastics.org/news/publications/). 
• In cooperation with academic and private scientific research institutes, EUBP annually publi shes a 
comprehensive bioplastics market data study (https://www.european-bioplastics.org/market/).

Infrastructure & technical equipment 
As the key platform for technical knowledge, industry information, contacts, and networking, EUBP has access to 
a significant network of decision makers in the world of bioplastics and a contact database for the association’s 
dissemination activities comprising over 8,000 contacts. 
Furthermore, EUBP is licensor of the Seedling® logo, an EN 13432-based conformity mark 
of industrial compostability for biodegradable plastic packaging. EUBP has created and owns 
the Seedling® mark of conformity for compostability of plastic packaging. EUBP continues to 
be involved in the supervision of the EN 13432 standard upon which European certificates of 
biodegradability of plastic packaging are based. Furthermore, EUBP is a member of several 
CEN and ISO committees dealing with plastics and packaging. EUBP provides authoritative 
input for all relevant standards on the European level. 
EUBP’s head office is located in the centre of Berlin.

4.1.24 University of Padova - Department of Economics and Management "Marco Fanno" 
Short Name UNIPD Type  RTD Country IT 
 
 
 https://www.economia.unipd.it 
 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
The University of Padua is one of Europe’s oldest and most prestigious seats of learning; it is a multi -disciplinary 
university that aims to provide its students with both professional training and a solid cultural background. A 
qualification from the University of Padua is a symbol of having achieved an ambi tious objective, one that is 
recognised and coveted by both students and employers alike. Courses at the University of Padua are constantly 
updated in order to meet the ever-changing needs of the labour market. Its Healthcare degrees, for instance, cover a 
wide range of new courses such as Pediatric Nursing (Medical School), or Neuroscience and Neuropsychological 
Rehabilitation (Psychology). Engineering degree programmes are available in the fields of Civil, Architectural, 
Environmental, Industrial and Info rmation Engineering. University of Padua degrees also reflect today’s needs to 
safeguard both the environment with courses in Environmental Sciences and Technology (Agriculture Sciences), 
and consumers with Safety and Hygiene of Food Products (Veterinary Medicine). Research into pharmaceuticals is 
also covered with Pharmaceutical Biotechnologies (Pharmacy), as is research into hi-tech products with a course in 
Materials Science (Sciences). Great emphasis is also placed on Humanities, such as History and Con servation of 
Artistic and Cultural Heritage (Arts and Philosophy), and on teacher training with a course in Primary Education 
(Education).The University’s traditional courses for professionals in Law, Economics, and Business Management 
are run alongside courses that analyse complex social systems such as Sociological Sciences (Political Sciences) and 
Statistics, Population and Society (Statistical Sciences). Furthermore, highly motivated University students may also 
apply for admission to the Galilean School of Higher Education. After a demanding selection process, each year 30 
students are chosen to attend the School’s high-level in-house courses and to use its special services. 
 
Overview of the Department of Economics and Management- Intro 
The Department of Economics and Management Marco Fanno (DSEA) was founded in 1989 and it soon became a 
leading centre in delivering high-quality research and teaching within the higher education Institutions in both fields 
of economics and business. Currently, the DSEA counts 67 faculty members, 25 admin staff and approximately 2000 
students. According to the Italian regulations, the working language of the Department is Italian, whereas the 
teaching offer is provided mainly in English.  As far as research is concerned, the DSEA was ranked fourth out of 
94 Departments at national level – according to the Valutazione Qualitativa della Ricerca (VQR) 2004 -10. About 
36% of publications were rated as 'excellent' compared to the average 18% at the national level. In the subsequent 
round of VQR (2011-14), the DSEA further improved its performance and has been ranked third out of the 48 mid-
sized departments in economics and business in Italy. The percentage of 'excellent' publications has further increased, 
totaling 50% of the total number of scientific products. The Italian Ministry of University and Research included the 
DSEA amongst the Departments of Excellence for the period 2018-22. In 2016 the University guide Grande Guida 
ranked DSEA at the first place among large universities for teaching quality in the areas of Economics and Statistics. 
Out of 850 Universities, our Department is also at the top of the U-Multirank international ranking.  
 
Description of the Activities at the Department of Economics and Management 
Since its foundation, DSEA has always placed a great emphasis to both teaching and research. In July 2016 DSEA 
was ranked in Italy for teaching quality by Censis. The ranking is based on several indicators measuring teaching 
quality and likeliho od for students to find good jobs. In addition, students are offered the opportunity to spend 
training periods in private firms, public institutions, research centres, and non -profit organizations. DSEA prides 
itself to being a leading and highly research-oriented institution: as a matter of fact, within DSEA there are scholars 
and research groups of recognized international value. This can be shown using different indicators adopted 
internationally to define the scientific performance in economics and business:  
(i) the quality of the journals in which the scientific works are published;  
(ii) the international dissemination/reputation of the research conducted; 
(iii) the presence of international scientific journals on editorial boards;  
(iv) the number of  invitations received by the faculty to give plenary/keynote lectures as well as appointments as 
visiting fellows at leading Institutions (University of Melbourne, Universitat Pompeu Fabra, Queensland University 
of Technology, Columbia Business School); 

DT-NMBP-04-2020    
 
[BIOMAC]   [85 of 115] 
(v) appointments to editorial boards of leading international journals in the various disciplines (e.g. Corporate 
Governance: an International Review; European Accounting Review; Accounting, Auditing and Accountability 
Journal; Family Business Review) 
The DSEA has also achieved remarkable results in terms of visibility and international diffusion of its research. 
Almost 70% of the publications presented by the DSEA in the last VQR were considered excellent or very good, 
obtaining an average score of 0.7 out o f 1. In relation to the international context, Padova ranks 108th on a global 
scale for the economics area in the URAP Field based ranking 2016 -17, third at national level. In the RUR 2016 
Research ranking, for the Social Sciences area, Padova ranks first in Italy and 214th internationally. In the Field 
Rankings of CWTS Leiden, Padova ranks first in Italy for the macro-area Social Sciences and Humanities, 130th in 
the world. Members of the DSEA are regularly involved into international networks. This network has been built up 
through the organization of high -profile weekly scientific seminars. During 2019, 54 scholars were invited, 47 of 
whom were affiliated to a foreign university. We also hosted in 2018 high -level researchers within our visiting 
scientists program. DSEA members actively participates in national and international competitive tenders. In the last 
round, one PRIN project was won (3 in the previous round). DSEA is the scientific partner for Italy of the European 
research infrastructure SHARE-ERIC. In this field it has received several funds from the European Commission. It 
is currently linked -third-party in the H2020 project "Achieving world -class standards in all SHARE countries — 
SHARE-DEV3" (Prof Weber), partner in the H2020 project "Synergies for Europe's Research Infrastructures in the 
Social Sciences — SERISS" (G. Weber) and participates in the COST -ACTION on "European Energy Poverty: 
Agenda Co-Creation and Knowledge Innovation". Finally, DSEA has been involved in projects of considerable 
international relevance such as, for example, the European SmartSpec Project, the cross -border PROFILI Project, 
the CLUSTRAT Project and has received significant funding from private foundations such as the JPMorgan 
Foundation, for the project "Research on underserved SMEs resilience strategies in the UK and in Europe" with 
University of Warwick (Prof Campagnolo). 
To further enhance high -quality research, in the last few years the department has embraced an important cultural 
shift emphasizing the importance  of systematic assessment and evaluation of research quality. The distribution of 
research funds for Research Grants and Research Projects is carried out on a competitive basis. Within this process 
a significant weight is assigned both to the scientific production of the Principle Investigator (and his research team) 
and to the degree of innovation of the project. These projects are evaluated by highly qualified external reviewers.  
Among the different research areas developed at DSEA ( https://www.economia.unipd.it/ricerca/ricerca) it is also 
included the topic of environmental and social sustainability and circular economy. 
Role in the Project 
UNIPD will start its contribution in WP5 related to Market uptake and Hub services. UPD lead Task 5.1: Workflow 
design and Preparatory Market Uptake  as well as Task 5.2: Innovation Management and Business plans by 
coordinating the management of innovation processes, business process, marketing and organizational innovation; 
as well as the coordination of investors, regional or national public investors as well as bank funds; pursuing private 
funding (investments), loans or public funding to support the development of BIOMAC.  UPD and the Department 
of Economics and Management has developed research and networks, and experience in business ecosystems, 
innovation processes, start-ups and business models, also in relation to environmental sustainability (with a focus on 
circular economy, business model innovation, implications in terms of eco -innovation in a circular economy 
framework). Within the project UPD will provide knowledge in order to elaborate business plans for the 5 selected 
cases included into the ecosystem mapped in order than to provide. By coordinating the other partners included into 
the task 5.2, UPD will identify commercialization opportunities as wel l as potential financial opportunities. There 
will be constant contact with the project coordinator, partners, actors involved in the pilot case studies and 
stakeholders. Additionally, UPD will lead WP8 related on the Sustainability and Exploitation of OIT B and within 
the WP also will be task leader for Task 8.2 Knowledge management and IP. UPD has lots of experience in dealing 
with distributed innovation processes and open innovation framework, together with IP management and technology 
transfer. From this  point of view UPD will coordinate the partners involved in the WP aiming at designing a 
sustainable management and institutional infrastructure able to guarantee the economic and financial sustainability 
of the results of the project. Moreover, by leveraging its competences and experience in market analysis and trends, 
ecosystem map and development as well as IP management, UPD will create the conditions and tools enabling 
knowledge transfer and ensure that the outputs of the projects could find adequate sustainability as far as market and 
financial elements are concerned. UPD has also developed over the years lots of research in innovation at the SME 
level as well as in multiple industries such as those included into the project. From this point of view, U PD will 
further contribute to the project. 
UPD will contribute to the WP9 Exploitation strategy of the ecosystem being in close communication with partners 
across the supply and value chain and more specifically with PLs and Test cases. UPD will also be in volved in the 
dissemination activities of WP9 targeting to communicate all the results to targeted audiences (tradeshows, 
exhibitions, community, stakeholders and other channels), in close collaboration with Task 9.2 leader. Publication 
of the ecosystem’s description and services, publication of links to other related projects and events worldwide,

social media presence, as well as the dissemination of the project´s results to external target groups such as 
professional training, webinars, presentations at conferences & fairs, organization of workshops and study tours, and

4.1.25 IRIS Technology Solutions SL 
Short Name IRIS Type  SME Country ES 
 
http://www.iristechnologygroup.com/ 
 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
IRIS Technology Group (http://www.iristechnologygroup.com/) is an advanced engineering Group that was 
established in Barcelona in 2007. Since 2011, it also operates from Dublin (Ireland) whereas the Barcelona office is 
referred to as IRIS Technology Solutions S.L. It specializes in the manufacture and integration of Process Analytical 
Technology (PAT)-based real-time quality monitoring solutions for the process industries and IoT systems for smart 
manufacturing, predominantly targeted at the food, pharmaceutical and chemical industries. In particular, our 
product line comprises proprietary state -of-the-art IR analyzers for at -line and in -line process monitoring. On the 
one hand, our solutions are based on the latest developments in photonics in the fields of MEMs, Near Infrared 
Spectroscopy, Hyperspectral Imaging, and Raman. On the other hand, we leverage ICTs, whereby we apply Machine 
learning, Artificial Intelligence and Data Mining techniques for predictive and active control, as well as for decision 
support systems. In addition to photonics -based analyzers, we also work with IoT sensors for enabling equip ment 
and machinery for smart manufacturing and transitioning industry to the Industry4.0 paradigm. Our solutions are 
cloud-based for mobility, remote monitoring and multi-site applications.  
Our Innovation Division which is governed by an Innovation Commit tee comprising Senior Management, and an 
Innovation Unit for managing and executing the company’s innovation roadmap, has 3 core strategic lines, for 
shaping the Factory of the Future: 
 
1. New optical photonics-based technologies and PAT systems for production process optimization 
2. ICTs (Artificial intelligence / machine learning, IOT & cloud platforms) 
3. Circular and Bio-based Economy: digitalization and waste valorization 
In addition, to running an internal R&D program, as well as carrying our various joint private projects with industry 
partners, our Innovation Division is highly experienced in working in collaborative R&D projects in H2020 (both as 
coordinators and partners), principally in the SPIRE, FoF, and BBI programs. The company was established in 2007 
and currently employs 60+ staff with a turnover of € 5 M. It is equipped with engineering workshops (3), food testing 
and wet chemistry laboratory, optics labs (2), and an electronics/telecommunications lab. IRIS is ISO 9001:2008 
certified and also is certified under UNE-EN-ISO 166002: Management Systems R&D&i. We are also certified by 
the local (Catalonian) government as a provider of technological R&D services (Tecnio Certification). IRIS is a 
member of the following sectorial networks: SPIRE, SPIE and SECPHO, in addition to regional industrial collectives 
such as Smart Space (association of companies and organizations that specialize in the ‘smartification’ of industry). 
IRIS has a matrix of multidisciplinary knowledge groups in the company with strong expertise in engineering and 
science. With its team and resources, including electronics, mechatronics, mechanical, optical, industrial design 
engineers, as well as specialists in system engineering, application programming and web development etc. the group 
can carry out full system design and engineering, including electronic design and assembly, firmware and software 
development, electrical harnesses and interconnections, mechanical design for enclosure and prototype integration, 
as well as instal lation, validation and industrialization of prototypes and equipment in production plants. As such 
they have recently delivered advanced plastic sorting devices. In addition to this broad cross-disciplinary engineering 
team, IRIS’ research team consists of data scientists, chemometricians, chemists and physicists, among others, who 
have the expertise to validate the technologies developed. 
Role in the Project 
IRIS is an engineering company, expert in process monitoring and evaluation through in-line monitoring. IRIS will 
provide monitoring systems to upgrade the capabilities of selected pilot lines. Particularly, IRIS will provide 
solutions to monitor the compositi on of the upstream biomass to be converted as well as solution for inline 
monitoring of PLs. IRIS will lead Task 2.2: Inline monitoring and AI of PLs providing tailored artificial intelligence 
models to use the data from the process monitoring to optimize the process. Further to this, IRIS will contribute to 
the dissemination and exploitation of the BIOMAC results.

Relevant product lines 
Monitoring devices for real-time quality control: 
• VisumPALM: NIR technology for incoming material quality control and detection of adulteration. 
• VisumNIR: In-Line NIR monitoring for product standardization and increase of production efficiency.

Partner Description 
Description of organization 
DIAD Group is a fast growing company in the sector of the advanced technologies, with a strong partnership all 
over the world, and find its success factor in the constant transformation of the knowledge produced by applied 
innovation into products, technologies and s ervices for the automotive and the manufacturing industrial sectors. 
Member of the Board of the Advanced Manufacturing Research Centre with Boeing (AMRC), one of most 
advanced facility for manufacturing technology in the world, located in Sheffield (UK), w here global players as 
Rolls Royce, Airbus, BAE, Mori Seiki, Bombardier, etc. are involved. Chair of the "Industrialisation and 
Nanomanufacturing" working group on the NANOFutures ETIP. Member of the Board of the International 
Research Center in Critical R aw Materials for Advanced Industrial Technologies (ICCRAM). The main 
activities of DIAD Group (short name DIGRO) are in the design, the development, the testing and the application 
of advanced components for the automotive and the aerospace sectors, using the most advanced engineering tools 
and innovative materials (like high performance composites, exotic materials, hyperfunctionalized surfaces, 
nanostructured based massive and coating materials). This target is achieved with a integrated approach that cover 
the design and engineering excellency and the setup of the related manufacturing technologies (intelligent and 
reconfigurable production systems and processing) always looking at the environmental aspects and the total life 
cycle approach. Our targeted customers and markets are large tier1 suppliers, high tech small and medium 
companies, and motorsport companies/teams, interested to sustainable and clean manufacturing and assembly of 
high tech components.  
Thanks to the large network of customers and industrial partners, the DIGRO exploitation capabilities are 
covering also other sectors like the new renewable energy, the eco-building, the industrial application of the 
nanotechnology and others. 
The DIAD Group offers a series of industrial and highly qualified engineering services:  
• Full design, development and zero series of advanced components and optimization of the related 
manufacturing systems, using innovative materials, custom technologies and state of the art functionalized 
surface engineering;  
• Development of technologies for  sustainable and clean manufacturing and assembly of high tech 
components;  
• Methods to reuse innovative materials;  
• Nanotechnology engineering to manufacturing and processing industry;  
• Product and Process Life Cycle and recovery /recycling methods;  
• Industrial implementation of energy saving policies;  
• Automotive testing of developed parts in extreme conditions and weather (like Nordic and desert climates); 
Role in the Project 
DIAD is a high -tech SME specialized in the design, testing, and application of advanced body parts for the 
automotive and motorsport sectors, using advanced engineering tools and innovative materials. This target is 
achieved with an integrated approach covering the design and engineering excellence and the setup of the related 
manufacturing technologies always looking at the environmental aspects and the total life cycle approach. DIAD 
will lead one of the 5 Test Cases that will be brought to the BIOMAC Eco system. In particular, DIAD will be 
responsible for Test Case 1: Automotive. BIOMAC intends to outperform state of the art components for interior 
use of the vehicle providing a bio -based nano reinforced solution to the sector. DIAD will set the requiremen ts 
(mechanical, surface finishing, aesthetic, customization, etc.) and the validation procedures to be applied (Task 
3.2).

4.1.28 Ohmatex A/S 
Short Name OHM Type  SME Country DK 
 
www.ohmatex.dk/ 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
Ohmatex A/S (OHM) is a privately-owned Danish engineering consultancy, entirely funded by customer projects and 
private capital. The company specialises in smart textile development, acting as advisors and development partners 
to textile businesses across the globe. Services include design and realisation of new products that  exploit the latest 
electronic technologies and fabric integration methods to add new functionality to textiles, and garments in particular. 
Founded in March 2004 with the aim of commercializing research developments and technologies in smart textiles 
and wearable electronics, Ohmatex has extensive experience with designing and prototyping textile-based electronics 
solutions, validation and establishment of commercially viable production strategies to provide clients with market -
ready products for a wide va riety of applications. Key competencies include development of smart monitoring 
garments, design and development of sensor electronics, integration of circuitry and power solutions exploiting 
moulded and 3D-printed encapsulation techniques to create washable and robust solutions. Ohmatex offers a range of 
solutions for connecting to textile-integrated electronics and circuitry, making the company ideally suited as a partner 
to specify prototypes and define test criteria for textile-based printed electronics solutions. 
Role in the Project 
Ohmatex has a multidisciplinary development team with backgrounds in electronics, textiles, mechanical design, and 
biomedical engineering. With more than a decade’s experience with smart garment development including electrical 
and mechanical design, fabric engineering and development of encapsulation and integration processes to match the 
mechanical properties of highly flexible and deformable textiles, Ohmatex will use these competencies in defining 
pilot plant services for bio -based conductive inks that can be printed directly into textiles (WP3, Task 3.6) where 
Ohmatex role will be in providing insights into end -user/market needs and validating developed services (WP4). In 
addition, a role is envisaged in the development of the value chain for services offered by the printed electronics hub 
where Ohmatex already offers relevant design, integration, and product prototyping services for smart textiles (WP6). 
The company would be an obvious partner to develop and provide solutions to connect to printed circuitry and 
electronics. 
Relevant publications, products to the project 
Ohmatex has been involved in designing and prototyping a number of sports and welfare wearables for commercial 
clients such as Palarum and Precure, as well as developing its own spin -out product for a muscle performance 
monitoring wearable from developments for the European Space Agency, ESA. For these development s, Ohmatex 
not only designed the concepts and system architectures, we built the prototypes, developed and integrated the control 
and data processing electronics, but also designed scalable manufacturing processes and establishing supply -chains. 
In some cases, Ohmatex also acts a supplier of assembled or semi-finished products to clients.

(https://cordis.europa.eu/project/id/248048)

4.1.29 EVERSIA INNOVA 
Short Name EVERSIA Type  LE Country ES 
 
www.eversia.es 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
EVERSIA INNOVA is a company specialized in Integral solutions in packaging and big manufacture of bags, waste 
bags and paper bags. Eversia was founded in 1979 by Romero´s Family. Last year Eversia closed 2019 year with a 
turnover of 82 M€ (20 M€ in export sales). In 2019 Eversia produced 40.000 ton of plastics and 5.000 of paper. We 
are working in the company about 350 people at the moment. Our facilities in Molina de Segura, Murcia, in the 
Southeast of Spain, cover more than 30,000 m2, produce more than 40,000 tons of plastic, 3,000 tons of paper and 
2,000 tons of film for automatic packaging, which are shipped by our costumers to millions of homes in 15 different 
countries. We have three main processes: 
• Plastics Extrusion 
• Plastics and Paper Printing  
• Paper and plastic Bags Converting.  
 
Eversia Innova has one of the most advanced Research and Development (R&D) departments in the country, since 
2010. Our lines of investigation are aimed at developing compostable and biodegra dable materials and also highly 
recyclable products, given our commitment to circular economy. Our research and innovation work are directed to 
design new innovating films, such as different standard materials coextrusion or bioplastics coextrusion; and 
implementing new methods and techniques that will help us gradually reduce the environmental impact of our 
activity. Eco -efficiency and sustainability are our two main lines of development.  Our Quality Assurance 
Laboratory is designed to guarantee the highest quality standards of all our products. Proof of it are the International 
standards certificates we have been awarded year after year: ISO 9001 / UNE 53942 / OK COMPOST / Blue Angel 
/ ISO 14001/ OHSAS 18001 / BRC Packaging./UNE 166002. This commitment can be seen in our Corporate Social 
Responsibility (CSR) aimed at creating social, workplace, economic, environmental and equal opportunities policies 
that focus on security, occupational health and safety, and environmental protection. 
Some of these policies are based on organisational flexibility, improvements in working conditions, and a balance 
of personal and professional life in the workplace . Our commitment to the world around us led us some years ago 
to develop a line of sustainable products called Ev ersiaBio. The EversiaBio brand is the most complete range of 
eco-friendly bags on the market. They are made to high environmental standards to ensure our products have 
optimum environmental qualities. These standards ensure our products have a very low environmental impact during 
their life cycle. 
Our personnel are highly qualified and work continually with universities (Universidad de Murcia, and Universidad 
Politécnica de Cartagena, etc.) and technology institutes (AIMPLAS (industrial plastics expertise), ITENE 
(packaging expertise), CETEC (footwear plastic expertise), CTC (food preservation expertise), etc.) to produce new 
products that satisfy demand in our sector. Our constant investment in technology and our new R&D and innovation 
projects place us at the forefront of the flexible packaging market. 
 
Eversia manufactures 40,000 tons of polymer annuallyin the following product types. A 3% of this production is 
bioplastic 
• Commercial bags (39 %) 3% bio 
• Rubbish (garbage) bags (32 %) 3% bio 
• Polymer film (food packaging) (11 %) <1% bio 
• Industrial segmented bags (9 %)<1% bio 
• Polymer coated paper for food packaging (3 %) <1%

Description of organization 
ACCIONA Construcción is a leading European construction company designing, constructing and managing 
buildings and civil infrastructures under sustainability principles. It has an international presence in more than 30 
countries and its turnover in 2019 was about 3430 million €, employing 11220 people. It is part of ACCIONA Group. 
ACCIONA business strategy is tightly linked to sustainability and in recognition of the company’s efforts and 
commitments Corporate Knights, a media group specializing in world -renowned sustainability rankings, has 
included ACCIONA, for the third year in a row, as one of the 100 most sustainable companies on the planet. 
ACCIONA uses cutting-edge technology to develop and apply the most advanced materials, components, systems 
and solutions for sustainability and in particular for developing added value infrastructures through better design and 
cost efficiency. In the whole life cycle, an area of prior interest is the enlargement of life span of new and existing 
infrastructure while reducing life cycle cost and environmental impact.

Role in the Project

main needs through the provision of renewable energy, infrastructure, water, and services. Within BIOMAC will 
lead Test Case 4: Construction. Based on their expertise, ACCIONA will set up the minimum req uirements; 
(mechanical and installation) needed to meet the strictest regulations of the construction market. ACCIONA will 
demonstrate/validate these 3D-printed composite elements in relevant industrial environments. ACCIONA will be 
also involved in dissemination, and exploitation activities of WP9 through its participation in European construction 
associations and standardization committees. In fact, through ACCIONA INNOVATION #Startups program 
innovative SMEs can obtain funding to execute a real pilot project in one of the businesses of the ACCIONA Group

Infrastructure & technical equipment 
Composites laboratory 
This laboratory is responsible for the manufacturing for all test pieces and composite scale prototypes developed in 
the technology center. The laboratory equipment is: Machining center, Micro -cutter for pieces cutting, Hot platen 
press for plastic, Panel lamination for the thermoplastic and th ermoset material processing cycles, Reactors for 
monomers polymerization. 
 
 
Physical Characterization facilities 
This laboratory is responsible for the mechanical tests for the characterization of different materials produced in the 
center of R & D, such as coatings, mortar, composite and polymeric materials. These tests are conducted by: Multi 
assays presses, Acquisition and monitoring of dynamic testing equipment for large structures, Durability aging 
testing machine. 
 
 
Materials laboratory 
It works in the characterization of polymers and composite materials by calorimetry, rheometry, thermogravimetry, 
infrared and chromatography. The laboratory equipment consists of: Differential scanning calorimeter, 
Thermogravimetric balance (TGA), IR and UV spectrophotometer, Rheometer to measure the behavior of liquid in 
response to applied forces and a viscometer with water bath and a muffle furnace.

4.1.31 NOVAMONT 
Short Name NVMT Type  LE Country IT 
 
 
www.novamont.com 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
Novamont is an Italian industrial company whose roots lie in the Montedison School of Materials Science and which 
was set up to implement the ambitious project of some researchers from the chemical corporation: to integrate 
chemistry, agriculture and the environment. Founded in 1989, it is now worldwide leader in the sector of 
biodegradable and compostable bioplastics and in the development of bioproducts. 
Novamont’s mission is to develop materials and biochemicals through the integration of chemistry and agriculture, 
by starting up biorefineries in the local areas and providing application solutions that ensure efficient use of resources 
throughout their entire life cycle, with advantages for the social, economic and environmental system. 
Its development model aims at building br idges between different sectors and creating new value by collaborating 
with all the stakeholders in the value chain: from agriculture to research, from industry to waste management, from 
local institutions to civil society. 
Guided by these principles, Novamont promotes an approach to bioeconomy based on the efficient use of renewable 
resources and on the regeneration of local areas, building world -first plants based on proprietary technologies and 
revitalising industrial sites that are decommissioned or no longer competitive to create new industries, new products 
and new jobs. Examples are Mater-Biotech, the company born from the reconversion of a decommissioned industrial 
site in north -east Italy into the first dedicated industrial plant at world level to produce biobutanediol through 
fermentative processes and Mater -Biopolymer, a plant located in central Italy which produces biodegradable 
biopolymers and is the resulted of the conversion of a PET production plant.  
Besides being an industrial company, Novamont is also a research centre which covers a wide range of expertise and 
specializations, with equipment and facilities ranging from laboratory scale activities to innovative pilot plants. Over 
the years it has developed five proprietary tech nologies for the production of bioplastics and bioproducts, creating 
synergies between the different areas of study (Bioplastics, Biotechnology, Agronomics and Organic Chemistry). 
Moreover, Novamont regularly implements training programs for young and expe rienced researchers, in 
collaboration with partners from the public and the private sector (more than 400 activities since 1996). 
Mater-Bi is the innovative family of bioplastics developed by Novamont research. It is biodegradable and 
compostable according to the European standard EN 13432 and other international standards and has characteristics 
of use very similar to those of traditional plastics. 
Mater-Bi provides solutions for specific environmental problems, such as soil and water pollution,while combining 
product quality and performance with an efficient use of resources. In particular, Mater -Bi has been conceived for 
applications in which biodegradability and compostability represent an added value, such as shopping bags that can 
be reused to collect organic waste or foodware products “contaminated” with leftovers, or serve a function, such as 
mulch films. The main fields of application are: separate waste collection, agriculture, large retail sector, disposable 
foodserviceware, packaging. 
With more th an 600 people, Novamont group posted sales of about €238 million in 2018 and made continuous 
investments in research and development activities: around 5% of its turnover, more than 20% of people (2018 
consolidated financial statements). It has a portfolio of around 1,800 patents and patent applications.  
The group has its headquarters in Novara, a production facility in Terni and research and development laboratories 
in Novara and Piana di Monte Verna (CE). Novamont’s subsidiaries are based in Porto Torres  (SS), Adria (RO), 
Terni and Patrica (FR). It has a representative office in Brussels (Belgium), foreign seats in Germany, France and 
the United States. It operates through own distributors in over 40 countries across all continents. 
At EU level, NOVAMONT is member of the BIC Consortium supporting the JTI Biobased Industry.  
At National level NOVAMONT is part of the founder members of SPRING, the National Technological Cluster on 
Green Chemistry, which in 2012 was officially acknowledged by the Italian Minister for Education and Research as 
a representative organization of the Italian sector of Green Chemistry. 
Role in the Project 
As an end-user of the project, Novamont’s role is to validate the biobased materials and biochemicals produced by 
various Pilot Lines. In particular, Novamont is leading Test Case 2: Agricultural Applications. In Task 3.3, 
Novamont will validate the production of biobased building blocks as monomers for the synthesis of biopolymers. 
Moreover, the biopolyesters will be processed by reactive extrusion incorporating other bionanomaterials produced 
in the PL platforms obtaining biodegradable and compostable bioplastics with suitable properties for applications in 
agriculture (e.g. for mulching films, pots, slow-release fertilizers, seeds coating, clips for pheromones release, etc.). 

DT-NMBP-04-2020    
 
[BIOMAC]   [104 of 115] 
In the WP2 Novamont will support the definition of the requirements for the mate rials in the PLs. Within the WP6 
Novamont will provide contribution to the LCA, LCC, and circularity assessment for the part of value chains where 
Novamont is directly involved (validation of building blocks and bionanomaterials for biodegradable and 
compostable bioplastics in agricultural applications). Novamont will perform activities to support the development 
of a plan for the exploitation of the results in the value chains where it is involved (WP8) by deploying, where 
needed, proper IP protection. Add itionally, Novamont will contribute the dissemination and communication 
activities (in conferences & fairs, and social media activities) in the WP9 and supporting the project management in 
the WP10. 
Relevant publications, products to the project 
In the years, Novamont developed a family of innovative bioplastics based on plant components and biodegradable 
polymers totally or partially obtained from renewable energy sources under the trademark Mater -Bi®. Novamont 
concentrates its application development activities in fields in which its products can make a tangible contribution 
to the efficiency with which the resources are used. As concrete proof of its constant research, Novamont counts a 
portfolio of about 1,000 patents. 
MATER-BI is the innovative family of bioplastics developed by Novamont research. It is biodegradable and 
compostable according to the European standard EN 13432 and other international standards and has characteristics 
of use very similar to those of traditional p lastics. MATER -BI provides solutions for specific environmental 
problems while combining product quality and performance with an efficient use of resources. In particular, 
MATER-BI has been conceived for applications in which biodegradability and compostab ility represent an added 
value, such as shopping bags that can be reused to collect organic waste or food ware products “contaminated” with 
leftovers, or serve a function, such as mulch films. The main fields of application are separate waste collection, 
agriculture, large retail sector, disposable food service ware, and packaging 
Previous Projects 
1. FIRST2RUN (H2020-BBI-PPP-2014-1-BBI-IA-FLAG): Flagship demonstration of an integrated biorefinery 
for dry crops sustainable exploitation towards biobased materials production, coordinated by Novamont and co-
funded by the BBI_JU. Low input oilseed cultures cultivated on arid and/or marginal land, are used to extract 
vegetable oils to be converted into biomonomers (primarily pelargonic and azelaic ac ids) and esters for the 
formulation of bioproducts such as biolubricants, cosmetics, plasticisers and bioplastics. Byproducts resulting 
from these manufacturing processes are further enhanced to obtain animal feed, other value -added chemicals 
and energy from scraps in order to increase the sustainability of the value chain. (GA No: 669029) 
2. DEEP PURPLE (H2020-BBI-JTI-2018): the project aims to transform diluted urban bio -wastes, including 
mixed waste streams, organic fraction of municipal solid waste, wastew ater and sewage sludge, into feedstock 
for bio-industry to obtain sustainable bio -products. This concept will be implemented in a novel Single -Site 
Multi-Platform Concept (Biomass, Cellulose and Biogas) to replace current polluting destructive practices with 
new value added concepts. The beneficial use of bio -waste is obtained by an innovative combination of 
optimized recovery technologies and novel solutions: the Purple Phototrophic Bacteria PhotoBiorefinery. The 
concept will be implemented by end-users from four municipalities, namely Madrid (ES), Toledo (ES), Třinec 
(CZ) and Velká Polom (CZ) to transform bio -wastes into high-added value bio-products: fine chemicals (bio -
cosmetics), fertilizers, bio-packaging and self-repairing construction materials. (GA No: 837998) 
3. GRACE ( H2020-BBI-JTI-2016. BBI-IA-DEMO): Demonstration and optimisation of the techno economic 
viability and environmental sustainability of ten pr omising miscanthus and hemp biomass -based value chains 
using marginal, contaminated and unused land at an industry relevant scale. The aim is to identify hemp varieties 
suitable for marginal lands and to have commercial miscanthus cultivars available by the end of the project with 
several proven economically viable end uses creating a market pull for growth in the bio -economy. (GA No: 
745012) 
4. FUNGUSCHAIN ( H2020-BBI-PPP-2015-2-1, BBI -IA-DEMO): The project aims at the valorization of 
agricultural residues com ing from mushroom (Agaricus Bisporus) farming residues as a case to set up new 
cascading possibilities using innovative procedures to extract high value bio -based additives (antioxidants, 
antimicrobials, proteins), convert lipids into bioplasticizers and p olysaccharides (glucans and fermentable 
sugars) into biopolymers using remaining side streams in substrates to close the agricultural cycle by composting 
and/or biogas synthesis. Fungushchain will demonstrate its industrial viability by building a new biorefinery that 
will use cost -effective extraction technologies (MAE and HWPE) revalorizing more than 65% of waste into 
valuable additives. (GA No: 720720) 
5. PERFORM (H2020-SPIRE02-2018): The technologies developed in PERFORM are directed towards highly 
efficient and integrated electrochemical systems which substantially improve oxidative chemical 
transformations based on bio-based feedstocks. PERFORM provides solutions for the need for the electrification 
of the chemical industry and establishes a flexible PowerPlatform pilot plant to be used also after the end of the 
project, allowing for continuing innovations and impact. Moreover, multi -step chemical conversions can be 
shortcut and performed in a single electrochemical cell, such that this can be considered a s a disruptive 
DT-NMBP-04-2020    
 
[BIOMAC]   [105 of 115] 
technology. Therefore, the implementation of electrochemical production methods for valueadded compounds 
is a game changer, leading to more efficient and sustainable production. (GA No 820723) 
Infrastructure & technical equipment 
Novamont plants involved in the project are: 
• Research laboratories and pilot plants (monomer and polymer synthesis, rheology, mechanical characterization, 
physical and chemical characterization, plastic materials transformation technologies, biodegradation, chemistry 
applied to vegetable oils, carbohydrates and lignocellulosic materials, biotechnology applied to chemicals, 
ecology of products and environmental footprint, engineering, agronomy), located in Novara. 
• Production plant (Mater -Bi® grades and Origo -Bi® polyesters from vegetable oils), laboratories (process 
engineering, quality control), compounding technology, oil treatment, polymer synthesis at a pilot plant level, 
located in Terni. 
• Biotechnology research centre in Piana di Monte Verna: Research ce ntre forming part of the Novamont 
Biotechnology Platform for the integration of chemical processes and industrial biotechnologies.

4.1.32 INSTITUTO DE SOLDADURA E QUALIDADE 
Short Name ISQ Type  RTO Country PT 
 
http://isq-group.com 
 
Partner Description 
Description of organization 
ISQ is an independent, private, non-profit, technical, scientific and industrial oriented organization founded in 1965 
with international presence in 16 countries, covering 4 continents. ISQ’s main activities include technical 
inspections, consultancy, tes ting, metrology, training and research and development in a wide range of technical 
areas such as materials, joining technologies, structural integrity and risk assessment, sustainability, eco and energy 
efficiency, health and safety, quality assurance, pr oduction technologies, industrial automation and robotics. ISQ 
provides support to different industrial sectors such as Process Industries, Energy (including renewables) and Oil 
&Gas, Aeronautical and Aerospace, Automotive, Construction and infrastructures , among others. It is one of the 
largest Portuguese technological infrastructures. ISQ’s know -how is supported by 16 accredited laboratories 
(accordingly with EN ISO/IEC 17025) and by a large involvement in National, European and International R&D 
projects, having participated in more than 400 R&D projects, in the last 30 years, in different funding programs 
(LIFE, LIFE+, RFCS, IEE, FP5, FP6, FP7, H2020), with a strong background of collaboration with a large number 
of Universities, Scientific Research Institutes, industrial companies and other institutions worldwide. Research and 
Development at ISQ supports all operational in-house technical areas in the enhancement of existing technologies 
and new solutions. It also encourages the development of breakthrough technologies and solutions that lead to new 
products/technologies/methodologies/services, promoting new Business areas and thus contributing to the 
technological development and competitiveness of the economy.  ISQ headquarters are at Porto Salvo, Oeira s, 
Portugal, with national delegations in Oporto, Castelo Branco, Loulé and Sines. At international level, ISQ is 
represented at: Angola, Brazil, Cape Verde, China, French Guiana, Mozambique, Norway, Saudi Arabia, Spain, 
United Arab Emirates, Turkey, Timor and USA. 
ISQ is a leading European Technological Infrastructure of applied research, a strong and reliable long -life partner 
for industry contributing to its technological development. ISQ has been selected by relevant scientific organisations 
as a competent and reliable partner to be involved in the main International Scientific projects as LHC-Large Hadron 
Collider (CERN), International Thermonuclear, Experimental Reactor (ITER), IXV - Intermediate eXperimental 
Vehicle (ESA) and E -ELT-Extremely Large Tel escope (ESO). The large experience and know -how of ISQ staff, 
allows us to face the future challenges in the ceaseless search for new solutions towards sustainability. ISQ has large 
experience in areas which are very relevant to BIOMAC namely, eco-efficiency methodologies, Life Cycle Analysis, 
nanosafety, risk assessment, artificial intelligence, optimization and decision support tools. ISQ has a long -term 
relationship with Industry, providing technical expertise, technological transfer, training, thus cont ributing to the 
improvement of its competitiveness and sustainability. ISQ participates in a number of International 
Networks/Associations namely The European Steel Technology Platform (ESTEP); European Technology Platform 
for advanced Engineering Material s and Technologies (EUMAT); Energy Materials Industrial Research Initiative 
(EMIRI); ENERGY IN; Production Technologies Cluster (PRODUTECH); Sustainable Process Industry Through 
Resource Efficiency (SPIRE), National Group for Process Integration (GNIP), Th e European Virtual Institute for 
Integrated Risk Management (EU -VRi); European technology platform on industrial safety (ETPIS); Portuguese 
Aeronautic, Space and Defense Cluster (AED Portugal), among others. 
Role in the Project 
ISQ will be involved in specific tasks in WPs  2, 4, 5 and 6. In WP2, ISQ will participate with special focus on Task 
2.2:  Inline monitoring and AI of PLs, and, Task 2.3: Process Control of PLs, namely in PLs 2,4,5,11 and 16, 
supporting the sensoring and the setting up of real-time monitoring of the designated PLs in order to improve improve 
process control and optimization. In WP4, ISQ will participate in Task 4.3 : Process Validation and predictive 
modelling, supporting the development of models emulating the system behaviour for the production lines (2, 4, 5, 
11 and 16) built from the combination of analytical correlations and collected data from the different pilots with the 
main purpose to produce a simulation environment (or digital twin of the process es) which advances data for the 
techno-economic and environmental assessment at the desired scale.  In WP5, ISQ will participate in Task 5.3 :  
Health and safety, Nanosafety, supporting the identification of the potential risks and uncertainties associated with 
exposure (human and environmental) to the proposed new solutions. This assessment will produce usable 
information on the potential occupational exposure associated with the production processes/technologies especially 

DT-NMBP-04-2020    
 
[BIOMAC]   [107 of 115] 
addressing all process.  In WP 6, ISQ will lead Task 6.2 - Life Cycle Assessment (LCA) and participate in Task 6.3: 
Life Cycle Cost (LCC). LCA will be undertaken for 5 relevant products to be developed in the test cases. The tasks 
include: (i) definition of the objectives, methodology, bou ndaries and technology indicators for the LCA/LCC, (ii) 
life cycle inventory, (iii) life cycle impact assessment (iv) analysis of LCA/LCC results and (v) critical raw materials 
assessment. Finally, ISQ will also be involved in the dissemination activities targeting to communicate all the results 
to targeted audiences (tradeshows, exhibitions, community, stakeholders and other channels). ISQ will promote and 
establish liaisons with relevant entities and initiatives related to sustainability and circular econ omy strategies, in 
order to promote synergies and knowledge exchange and to foster potential partnerships to strengthen both the 
BIOMAC ecosystem and its clients.
